PAGE 52 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 Version 5.0.0
3. Requirements for permanent safety barriers
3.76.1
VRS should be placed a minimum of 10 m from the back of the nose.
NOTE 1
Where street furniture and other hazards are located close to the back of the nose, it can be difficult to
provide the minimum length of need of safety barrier in advance of the hazards and/or provide the
required permanent lateral displacement zone for the crash cushion.
NOTE 2
Traffic on an adjacent slip or link road that is following a broadly parallel alignment and similar level to
the mainline carriageway is not seen as a hazard to traffic on the mainline carriageway, and vice versa.
Safety barrier provision in central reserves - general
3.77
Where the distance across the central reserve between the points from which set-back for each
carriageway is measured (i.e. Psb to Psb) is 10m or less, a central reserve safety barrier shall be
provided.
3.78
Where the distance Psb to Psb across the central reserve is more than 10m, the RRRAP [Ref 81.N]
shall be used to determine the need for, location and extent of safety barrier(s) and their minimum
containment level based on:
1)
the hazards that are present and their location;
2)
the intervening topography; and
3)
the likelihood of a vehicle crossing to the other carriageway.
3.79
The Overseeing Organisation's specific requirements for the minimum containment level and
performance of the central reserve safety barrier shall apply.
NOTE
The Overseeing Organisation's specific requirements for the minimum containment level and
performance of central reserve safety barrier are provided in the National Application Annexes.
3.80
Where a safety barrier in the central reserve is required, it shall be provided on both sides of a hazard
except:
1)
where the topography of the central reserve makes it impossible for the hazard to be reached
from one carriageway, or
2)
where the Overseeing Organisation agrees that lighting columns, signals or signs, passively safe
or fully collision resistant gantry legs or signs are permitted to be mounted on the top of the
central reserve safety barrier.
3.80.1
A double-sided barrier which provides vehicle containment on both carriageways may be used instead
of two separate lengths of single sided safety barrier adjacent to both carriageways, so long as the
traffic face presented to both carriageways is in accordance with the manufacturer's product description
and associated installation instructions.
3.81
Where localised widening of a concrete safety barrier is required by the manufacturer's product
description and associated installation instructions to accommodate the attachment of lighting columns,
signals or signs, passively safe or fully collision resistant gantry legs or signs on to the top of it,
localised widening shall be provided as a design output.
3.81.1
Where localised widening of a concrete safety barrier is required to accommodate the attachment of
lighting columns, signals or signs, passively safe or fully collision resistant gantry legs or signs on to the
top of it, it may be necessary to increase the width of the concrete safety barrier over a longer length
(i.e. not just locally) so as to provide a smooth and flowing alignment to the concrete safety barrier.
3.82
Where a sign plate greater than 2 m in height is located in a position where the bottom of the sign plate
is less than 1.5 m above the adjacent carriageway, and is mounted on top of a concrete barrier; the
extremities of the sign face or signal face shall not exceed the narrowest section of the concrete safety
barrier on which it is mounted.
3.82.1
To ensure that the extremities of the sign face or signal face do not exceed the narrowest section of the
concrete safety barrier on which it is mounted, the width of the concrete safety barrier may need to be
increased locally.
51
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

PAGE 53 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 Version 5.0.0
3. Requirements for permanent safety barriers
3.83
Any transition from a standard width to a wide width of concrete safety barrier shall be in accordance
with the manufacturer's product description and associated installation instructions.
3.84
Where a safety barrier is required and there are no hazards in the central reserve and there is a
difference in the opposing edge of carriageway levels of 200 mm or more and a slope steeper than 1 in
20 between carriageways, safety barrier shall be installed adjacent to both carriageways.
3.85
Where the topography of the central reserve makes it possible for the hazard to only be reached from
one carriageway, the safety barrier shall be only be placed on that side of the hazard.
3.86
Where a single sided safety barrier in the central reserve is located in a position where it is possible for
it to be struck on the non traffic face, a separate safety barrier shall be located adjacent to the opposite
carriageway.
Requirements for gaps in the central reserve safety barrier
3.87
There shall be no gaps in the central reserve safety barrier on motorways or on roads constructed to
motorway requirements other than where it has been determined that no safety barrier is required.
3.88
Existing gaps in central reserve safety barriers shall be closed unless they are required to remain open
for the operation, management and or maintenance of the road.
General requirements for an emergency crossing point/maintenance crossing
point (ECP/MCP)
3.89
An emergency crossing point/maintenance crossing point (ECP/MCP) shall only be installed with the
approval of the Overseeing Organisation.
3.90
Design drawings shall be produced showing the ECP/MCP in both the open and closed configurations.
NOTE
For the majority of the time, the ECP/MCP is in the closed configuration and hence, is required to
function as a permanent safety barrier.
3.91
Where an ECP exists on a road which is to be improved or when other works (excluding routine
maintenance) are being carried out, an assessment shall be undertaken to confirm the need for the
ECP to be retained with the Overseeing Organisation and relevant Emergency Services.
3.92
An ECP shall have a maximum length of 25 m and be designed using a location specific swept path
analysis.
NOTE
An ECP can be located in either the central reserve, or in the verge.
3.93
Any location specific requirements for the ECP/MCP shall be included as a design output, such as
maximum acceptable time taken for opening and closing, and storage requirements whilst the
ECP/MCP is open (where applicable).
NOTE 1
An opening time of 30 minutes or less is acceptable for an ECP.
NOTE 2
Guidance on factors relating to ECPs and MCPs is given in Appendix D of this document.
Use of removable barrier sections (RBS) at an ECP/MCP
3.94
The requirements of Section 10 shall apply to RBS used at an ECP/MCP.
Use of demountable permanent barrier at an MCP
3.95
For an MCP, the permanent safety barrier shall be demounted, the operations requiring the demounting
of the permanent safety barrier conducted, and the permanent safety barrier reinstated, within one shift.
3.95.1
Socketed posts may be included as a design output to allow the permanent safety barrier to be
dismantled and reinstated quickly.
NOTE
The time for the dismantling and reinstatement of barriers varies depending on the safety barrier and, if
used, can mean a lot of repair work to reinstate the safety barrier.
52
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

3. Requirements for permanent safety barriers
3.96
With the exception of emergency usage, whenever a section of safety barrier is demounted, the ends of
the safety barrier shall be made safe.
NOTE
The risk to road users from the exposed end of a safety barrier can be reduced through the use of
terminals, crash cushions, transitions and/or an RBS.
Additional requirements for "open" ECPs
3.97
Retained "open" ECPs shall be closed with a row of suitable traffic cylinders of at least 600 mm in
height.
3.97.1
Retained "open" ECPs should be gated.
3.98
Traffic cylinders used in retained "open" ECPs shall be spaced at a maximum of 1.0m centres between
the end terminals of the safety barriers.
3.99
The alignment of the two opposing sections of safety barrier and their end terminals at an "open" ECP
(or other open central reserve crossing point) shall be such that a vehicle impacting the safety barrier
prior to the gap is directed away from and not towards the leading terminal of the downstream safety
barrier.
3.100
At "open" ECPs, the terminal specification shall be in accordance with Section 6 of this document.
NOTE
Typical arrangements for safety barrier at approaches to an Emergency Crossing Point in the central
reserve, are shown in Figure 3.100N.

3. Requirements for permanent safety barriers
Additional requirements for maintenance crossing points (MCP) and maintenance access
3.101
Where MCPs (see CD 192 [Ref 78.N]) are provided to facilitate contraflow traffic flows during schemes
and tunnel maintenance, the layout shall be such that the open and closed layouts and the deployment
of an RBS do not present additional hazards to the road user or road worker.
3.102
Allowance shall be made in the length of the RBS included as a design output for any impact resistant
terminal end to the safety barrier.
3.103
Where the regular routine maintenance regime requires short period contraflow operation, the safety
barrier used to close the gap shall have a minimum containment level equal to that of the adjacent
safety barrier.
3.104
Where the regular routine maintenance regime does not require short period contraflow operation, on
completion of the works, any MCP gap(s) shall be closed by re-instating the original safety barrier(s) in
accordance with the manufacturer's product description and associated installation instructions.
3.105
Any 'above ground' elements of the temporary end termination(s) of the safety barrier shall be removed.
3.106
Transitions shall be used between the permanent sections of safety barrier and RBS and temporary
end termination(s).
Winter maintenance crossing points (WMCP)
3.107
Where directed by the Overseeing Organisation, a central reserve WMCP shall be provided.
3.108
The WMCP shall preclude unauthorised access or use.
3.109
The central reserve at a WMCP shall safely accommodate the movement between carriageways of all
winter maintenance vehicles and associated equipment likely to be deployed.
3.110
Signs and traffic cylinders complying with Diagram 7103 of UKSI 2016/362 [Ref 82.N] and of the NISR
1997/386 (TSRNI) [Ref 86.N] at 1.0m (maximum) centres shall be placed within the WMCP and either
side of any RBS that is installed to limit misuse of the WMCP.
Emergency Crossing Rapid Access Point (ECRAP)
3.111
The requirements for ECPs shall apply to ECRAPs, unless alternative requirements are given in this
section.
3.112
ECRAPs shall meet the typical fire and rescue service vehicle access route specification requirements
of Table 15.2 of Building Regs Doc. B2 [Ref 4.N].
3.112.1
The design of the opening in the ECRAP may be such that it does not permit directional flow.
3.113
Where it is necessary for an emergency vehicle to manoeuvre after passing through an ECRAP,
sufficient space shall be available for the emergency vehicle manoeuvre to be completed.

CD 377 Version 5.0.0
4. Requirements for vehicle parapets
4.
Requirements for vehicle parapets
General requirements for vehicle parapets
4.1
Vehicle parapets shall be provided on bridges and structures where a safety risk assessment
determines that there is a risk of an errant vehicle falling from a vertical or near vertical drop that is not
protected by a safety barrier or other suitable restraint.
4.1.1
In addition, vehicle parapets may be required to protect the area below the bridge or structure from
vehicle incursion.
4.1.2
The assessment and upgrading of in-service vehicle parapets should be carried out according to the
requirements in CS 461 [Ref 2.N].
NOTE 1
A vehicle parapet typically extends along the full length of a bridge deck (including the wing-walls)
and/or along the full length of any other structure.
NOTE 2
Where two structures are close together, a vehicle parapet can extend beyond the length of the
structures if it is impractical to transition to safety barriers between the two structures.
Minimum containment level requirements for vehicle parapets where the road is
not carried over or adjacent to a railway
4.2
On roads with a speed limit of 50 mph or more, the minimum containment level for vehicle parapets
shall be N2 unless a site specific risk assessment identifies that a minimum containment level greater
than N2 is required.
4.3
On roads with a speed limit of less than 50 mph, the minimum containment level for vehicle parapets
shall be N1 unless a site specific risk assessment identifies that a minimum containment level greater
than N1 is required.
4.4
A site specific risk assessment shall include the output from the RRRAP [Ref 81.N].
NOTE
A site specific risk assessment can include, for example, the output from a CS 453 [Ref 75.N] or a CS
461 [Ref 2.N] risk assessment.
4.5
Where a site specific risk assessment identifies that a containment level greater than the minimum level
is required, the greater containment level shall be included as a design output.
4.6
Where a site specific risk assessment identifies that a very high containment level is required, an H4a
containment vehicle parapet shall be included as a design output.
4.7
Where the need for a higher containment level or very high containment level vehicle parapet has been
identified, the nature of the risk, any mitigation with the steps taken to reduce the risk and the resulting
containment level required shall be recorded.
Minimum containment level requirements for vehicle parapets where the road is
carried over or adjacent to a railway
New bridges and structures (except accommodation bridges)
4.8
On a new bridge or structure (except accommodation bridges) over or adjacent to a railway, an H4a
containment level vehicle parapet shall be provided, regardless of the road class.
Existing bridges and structures (except accommodation bridges)
4.9
On an existing bridge or structure (except accommodation bridges) over or adjacent to a railway, an
H4a containment level vehicle parapet shall be provided, regardless of the road class.
4.9.1
Where an H4a parapet is not provided on an existing bridge or structure (except accommodation
bridges) over or adjacent to a railway, the highest containment provision possible should be provided,
which incorporates the output from the RRRAP and the feasibility of providing a suitable support
structure.
56
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025



======================================================================
PAGE 58 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 Version 5.0.0
4. Requirements for vehicle parapets
4.9.2
The containment level may be provided by a new vehicle parapet (preferred) or by a length of safety
barrier installed in front of the existing vehicle parapet.
4.10
An assessment shall be undertaken to determine whether modification of the structure is viable in order
to provide a suitable supporting structure, and an approval in principal obtained in accordance with CG
300 [Ref 73.N].
4.11
Where an H4a parapet is not provided on an existing bridge or structure (except accommodation
bridges) over or adjacent to a railway, the vehicle parapet containment level shall not be lower than the
normal containment level.
4.12
Where an H4a parapet is not provided on an existing bridge or structure (except accommodation
bridges) over or adjacent to a railway, agreement shall be sought through early engagement with the
Railway Authority and the Overseeing Organisation.
New and existing accommodation bridges
4.13
On new and existing accommodation bridges over or adjacent to a railway, the minimum vehicle
parapet containment level shall be normal containment level unless a site specific risk assessment
identifies that a minimum containment level greater than normal containment level is required.
4.14
On new and existing accommodation bridges over or adjacent to a railway, where a site-specific risk
assessment indicates that a containment level higher than the minimum level is required, the higher
containment level shall be included as a design output following confirmation from the Overseeing
Organisation and the Railway Authority.
4.15
On new and existing accommodation bridges over or adjacent to a railway, where the need for a higher
containment level or very high containment level vehicle parapet has been identified, the nature of the
risk, any mitigation with the steps taken to reduce the risk and the resulting containment level required
shall be recorded.
Impact severity level (ISL) for vehicle parapets
4.16
The ISL for vehicle parapets shall be either ISL A or ISL B.
4.16.1
ISL A should be selected over ISL B as it affords a lower level of injury risk to the occupants of an
errant vehicle than ISL B.
Normalised working width class and normalised vehicle intrusion class for
vehicle parapets
4.17
For normal containment level vehicle parapets, the maximum identified value of normalised working
width class that the local hazard(s) allow, shall be included as a design output.
4.18
For higher and very high containment level vehicle parapets, the maximum identified values of
normalised working width class and normalised vehicle intrusion class that the local hazard(s) allow,
shall be included as design outputs.
4.19
The vertical drop at the edge of the bridge deck shall be outside of the normalised working width of the
vehicle parapet unless the vehicle parapet was tested to BS EN 1317-1 [Ref 62.N] and BS EN 1317-2
[Ref 61.N] with a simulated bridge deck edge behind the vehicle parapet.
4.19.1
Where the edge of the bridge deck is within the normalised working width of the vehicle parapet in the
design, the distance between the traffic face of the vehicle parapet and the edge of the bridge deck
should be less than or equal to the distance in the full-scale impact test.
Length of need for vehicle parapets
4.20
The length of need for each vehicle parapet shall be given as a design output.
4.21
Where the total length of vehicle parapet provision requires the use of different parapets with different
essential characteristics due to output from the RRRAP [Ref 81.N], the length of need of each parapet
shall be detailed separately as a design output.
57
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

PAGE 59 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 Version 5.0.0
4. Requirements for vehicle parapets
4.22
Where a higher containment level or a very high containment level vehicle parapet is required at a
hazard adjacent to the vehicle parapet, and the hazard is such that other parties could be affected, the
length of the higher or very high containment parapet shall extend to the lesser of:
1)
the length of the bridge deck and the full length of the wing-walls where they broadly follow the
road alignment, or along the full length of the structure where it runs alongside and/or over the
adjacent hazard;
2)
on two-way carriageways, the distance between a position 25 m in advance of the point of no
recovery (PNR) in each direction i.e. 25 m plus the length of the adjacent hazard between the
PNRs, plus 25 m (refer to Figure 4.22a); or
3)
on one-way carriageways, the distance between a position 25 m in advance of the PNR in the
approach direction and a position 10 m after the PNR in the departure direction (refer to Figure
4.22b).

requirements (two way carriageways)

4.22.1
On a structure spanning more than one adjacent hazard, where the higher containment or very high
containment level vehicle parapet extents from clause 4.22(2) or clause 4.22(3) do not overlap or
extend to the limits in clause 4.22(1), normal containment level parapet with suitable transitions may be
used over the intermediate length(s) so long as the intermediate length meets the manufacturer's
requirements for minimum/maximum installation length (refer to Figure 4.22.1).
Figure 4.22.1 Localised higher or a very high vehicle parapet containment

4.23
Where the length of need for each hazard overlaps and the required containment levels differ, the

highest level of containment shall take precedent over the lower level of containment (refer to Figure

Figure 4.23 Localised higher or a very high vehicle parapet containment

Minimum height of vehicle parapets
4.24
The height of vehicle parapets (including combined vehicle/pedestrian parapets) shall not be less than
1000mm.
NOTE
A higher vehicle parapet height can be required due to the need for additional suicide prevention
measures and/or the requirements of other design documents.
4.25
For cycling routes immediately adjacent to the vehicle parapet and for accommodation bridges, the
minimum height of the vehicle parapet shall be 1500mm.
4.26
For very high containment level applications that are not over or adjacent to a railway, the minimum
height of the vehicle parapet shall be 1500mm.
4.27
For horse-riding routes immediately adjacent to the vehicle parapet, the minimum height of the vehicle
parapet shall be 1800mm.
4.28
For all bridges and structures over railways, the minimum height of the vehicle parapet shall be
1800mm.
4.29
The height of vehicle parapets (including combined vehicle/pedestrian parapets) shall be measured
above the adjoining paved surface.
4.30
The minimum height of a vehicle parapet (including combined vehicle/pedestrian parapets) shall be
given as a design output.
4.31
At particular sites where an aesthetic appraisal document as outlined in CD 351 [Ref 77.N] has been
undertaken, any height and form of vehicle parapet requirements so determined shall be agreed with
the Overseeing Organisation and any other responsible authority, and given as a design output.
NOTE
Any other responsible authority can include the Railway Authority/Environment Agency/Canal and
River Trust.
4.32
When it is necessary to increase the height of an existing legacy vehicle parapet, any extension shall
be compatible with, and not be detrimental to, the performance of the vehicle parapet system to which it
is attached.
60
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025



======================================================================
PAGE 62 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 Version 5.0.0
4. Requirements for vehicle parapets
4.32.1
The additional height may be provided by the use of a suitable additional non-participating structural
extension to the vehicle parapet (designed neither to become detached under impact nor participate in
containment and redirection of the vehicle).
4.32.2
The addition of a non-participating structural extension to a legacy vehicle parapet should be confirmed
as acceptable by the manufacturer/promoter of the vehicle parapet system, where the
manufacturer/promoter of the system still exists.
4.32.3
The addition of a non-participating structural extension to a legacy vehicle parapet should be confirmed
as acceptable by the Overseeing Organisation, where the manufacturer/promoter of the vehicle
parapet system no longer exists.
4.32.4
Where repair parts are available and the increased height variant of the vehicle parapet exists, the
change in height should be achieved by the exchange of standard parts compliant with the original
manufacturer's specification.
4.33
When it is necessary to increase the height of an existing UKCA/CE marked vehicle parapet, any
extension shall not invalidate the Declaration of Performance for the vehicle parapet to which it is
attached.
4.34
Where the height of an existing vehicle parapet is to be increased, the effect of any additional loading
on the supporting structure as a result of this modification, shall be assessed and remedial measures
undertaken, where necessary.
Verges on bridges and structures to accommodate vehicle parapets
4.35
The crossfall of any designed verge which is the potential location for a walking, cycling or horse riding
route shall be in the region of 5% (1 in 20), but no more than 10% (1 in10), and no less than 2.5% (1 in
40).
4.35.1
Where there is no access permissible, the crossfall of any designated verge may be increased to 20%
(1 in 5).
NOTE
The design of verges on bridges and structures is covered within CD 143 [Ref 17.N], CD 127 [Ref 12.N]
and CD 524 [Ref 18.N].
4.36
Any gradient of the verge shall meet the vehicle parapet manufacturer's product description and
associated installation instructions.
Plinth upstands
4.37
Where metal vehicle parapets are proposed, a plinth upstand of 50mm in height with a tolerance of
-0/+50mm shall be included as a design output.
NOTE
Not having a plinth affects the overall vehicle parapet height and rail positions relative to vehicle impact.
4.37.1
An upstand to aid drainage and/or reduce the amount of small stones and other debris kicked over the
edge of the bridge, should be included as a design output.
Vehicle parapets on historic monuments and bridges
4.38
Where a structure is subject to a cultural heritage management plan (refer to LA 116 [Ref 13.N]), the
parapet shall be managed in accordance with the conservation strategies of CG 304 [Ref 6.N].
4.38.1
New and replacement vehicle parapets on historical monuments and bridges may be designed from
first principles to meet the requirements of the cultural heritage asset management plan and the
particular performance class requirements.
Infilling of vehicle parapets
4.39
Where there is regular pedestrian access, vehicle parapets shall not provide toe-holds nor have
projections that would assist climbing of the vehicle parapet.
61
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025



======================================================================
PAGE 63 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 Version 5.0.0
4. Requirements for vehicle parapets
4.40
A solid infill panel with a minimum height of 600 mm measured above the adjoining paved surface shall
be provided at the bottom of a vehicle parapet where there is a horse-riding route adjacent to the
vehicle parapet.
4.41
Where solid panel or perforated sheets are proposed as infilling, the effect of wind loading on the
structure to which the parapet is attached shall be assessed in accordance with BS EN 1991-1-4 [Ref
23.N] and NA to BS EN 1991-1-4 [Ref 89.N].
4.42
Where infilling of a vehicle parapet is required, the infilling shall meet the requirements of BS 6779-1
1998 [Ref 37.N], as amended by Appendix E of this document.
4.42.1
Vibration resistant fixings should be preferred for the attachment of infilling to the vehicle parapet.
4.43
Where infilling of a vehicle parapet is required, this shall be given as a design output.
Provision of vehicle parapets on a divided structure
4.44
Where the longitudinal gap between the two decks on a divided structure is less than 100 mm, vehicle
parapets shall not be installed in the central reserve, unless warranted by risk assessment.
4.45
Where the longitudinal gap between the two decks on a divided structure is between 100 mm and 2 m, a
horizontal grid or slab or plate designed in accordance with BS EN 1991-2 [Ref 21.N] shall be provided.
4.46
Where the longitudinal gap between the two decks on a divided structure over a railway is between 100
mm and 2 m, the gap shall be infilled by a solid slab or plate designed with BS EN 1991-2 [Ref 21.N] to
carry special types general order and special order vehicles loading, irrespective of the type of VRS.
4.47
Where the longitudinal gap between the two decks on a divided structure is more than 2 m, vehicle
parapets shall be provided on each structure.
Additional requirements for vehicle parapets over or adjacent to railways
4.48
Assessment shall confirm local overhead line equipment clearances and / or trespass risk through early
liaison with the Railway Authority, British Transport Police or any other Police Authority.
4.49
The risk of road vehicle incursion at public and non-public sites in the following scenarios shall be
subject to an additional risk assessment in accordance with NR/L3/CIV/00012 [Ref 65.N]:
1)
Overbridge sites carrying single carriageway roads, dual-carriageway roads and motorways;
2)
Neighbouring sites where road and rail are beside each other; or
3)
Areas adjacent to a railway line where vehicles regularly park.
4.50
Vehicle parapets on new structures over or adjacent to railways shall comply with the Railway Authority
requirements for height, electrical clearance and protection; refer to NR/L3/CIV/020 [Ref 14.N]
incorporating NR/BS/LI/331 [Ref 56.N] and/or any successor documents.
4.51
Where vehicle parapets on existing bridges and structures over or adjacent to a railway are to be
replaced, reconstructed or strengthened, the location specific vehicle parapet height requirement and
electrical clearance and protection requirements shall be met.
4.52
Vehicle parapets on new structures over or adjacent to railways shall comply with the Railway Authority
requirements for steeple copings; refer to NR/BS/LI/331 [Ref 56.N] and/or any successor documents.
Infilling of parapets over railways
4.53
Infilling for vehicle parapets on bridges or structures over or adjacent to railways shall meet with the
requirements of BS EN 12676-1 [Ref 1.N], and this section.
NOTE
Where reference is made in BS EN 12676-1 [Ref 1.N] to "where electrification is likely" this denotes
electrification included within the Railway Authority's Investment Programme current at the time when
the vehicle parapet provision is being considered.

4. Requirements for vehicle parapets
4.54
Metal vehicle parapets of open construction shall have full height smooth solid infill which meets the
requirements of BS 6779-1 1998 [Ref 37.N], as amended by Appendix E of this document, where the
parapet is over or adjacent to a railway.
4.54.1
Metal vehicle parapets should be provided with additional solid sheeting on the outer (non-traffic) face
of the vehicle parapet/vehicle parapet posts.
4.54.2
The additional solid sheeting on the outer (non-traffic) face of the vehicle parapet/vehicle parapet posts
should extend vertically to the full height of the vehicle parapet, with the lower part shaped to cover the
outer ledge, and horizontally for at least the greater of one panel length, or 2m.
4.54.3
The additional solid sheeting on the outer (non-traffic) face of the vehicle parapet/vehicle parapet posts
should be fitted at the ends of the vehicle parapet or on both sides of the railway tracks.
4.55
The outer ledge of a vehicle parapet shall not be accessible from any area adjacent to the bridge.
4.55.1
Sheeting may be extended for situations where the outer ledge is accessible from any area adjacent to
the bridge.
4.56
All methods of preventing access to the outer ledge of the vehicle parapet shall be subject to the
agreement of the Railway Authority and the Railway Inspectorate.
4.57
The vehicle parapet, the infill sheeting and all conductive (metal) components shall be at least 3m from
the outer limit of any railway tracks or any live overhead electrification equipment.
Design and assessment requirements for vehicle parapets and supporting
structures
4.58
Main structural members of bridges shall not be designed to act as vehicle parapets.
NOTE
The design requirements given in this document for vehicle parapets are based on a cantilever action
from the bridge deck.
4.59
The resistance of the member supporting the vehicle parapet shall be assessed in accordance with CS
454 [Ref 3.N].
4.60
Any need to modify a bridge or structure to accommodate a UKCA/CE marked vehicle parapet shall be
reviewed in accordance with CS 451 [Ref 71.N].
4.61
Where is it found necessary to to modify a bridge or structure to accommodate a UKCA/CE marked
vehicle parapet, the bridge or structure shall be modified so that the member supporting the vehicle
parapet meets the requirements of the vehicle parapet manufacturer's product description and
associated installation instructions.
NOTE 1
For existing bridges and structures, the preference is to provide a UKCA/CE marked vehicle parapet
that is compatible with the existing site specific restrictions.
NOTE 2
It can be uneconomical or undesirable, perhaps for aesthetic reasons, to strengthen an existing
structure to take a vehicle parapet of the required containment level and normalised working width
class and, for higher or very high containment safety barrier, normalised vehicle intrusion.
NOTE 3
It can also be uneconomical or undesirable to strengthen the verge of the bridge deck to take the full
vehicle loading requirements.
NOTE 4
If so, strengthening to allow provision of a safety barrier between the existing parapet and edge of
carriageway, meeting the requirements of this document for containment level and normalised working
width class and, for higher or very high containment safety barrier, normalised vehicle intrusion,
requirements of this document between the existing parapet and edge of carriageway can warrant
investigation.
NOTE 5
Alternatively, the use of a safety barrier with integrated pedestrian restraint can warrant investigation.
4.61.1
In cases where it is decided to provide a safety barrier (meeting the containment, working width and, for
higher or very high containment safety barrier, normalised vehicle intrusion, requirements of this
63
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

CD 377 Version 5.0.0
4. Requirements for vehicle parapets
document) between the existing vehicle parapet and the edge of carriageway, the existing vehicle
parapet may be deemed to be a pedestrian parapet in accordance with this document.
4.62
For structures with non-carriageway elements that are unsuitable for unrestricted live loading, the
assessment shall determine the suitability of intermediate VRS with reference to CS 470 [Ref 41.N].
Anchorages and structural loading from vehicle parapets
4.63
The structure and plinth supporting the vehicle parapet shall be designed in accordance with the
loading requirements given in BS EN 1991-2 [Ref 21.N].
4.64
The design of anchorages for use in concrete shall meet the requirements of BS EN 1992-4 [Ref 25.N].
4.65
Removal and replacement of damaged sections of the vehicle parapet shall be readily achievable,
without damage to the supporting structure.
4.66
The design shall allow for the replacement of holding down bolts or sleeved threaded bar.
4.67
Loads applied to the supporting structure by the vehicle parapet potentially have to be estimated, and
any limitations arising shall be clearly identified.
NOTE
Where loads applied to the supporting structure by the vehicle parapet have been determined by
impact testing and / or experimental testing, this information can be used to assess the limitations of
the supporting structure.
4.68
The loading and anchorage requirements that the structure is capable of meeting shall be included as a
design output so that a compliant vehicle parapet and its associated anchorages are selected.
4.69
Where a vehicle parapet system complying with the minimum containment level, normalised working
width and, for higher or very high containment parapets, normalised vehicle intrusion class
requirements but imparting loads on the structure exceeding those included as a design output is
proposed, the adequacy of the proposed anchors shall be checked and calculations undertaken to
confirm that the structure is capable of resisting, without damage, all loads which the vehicle parapet
system is theoretically capable of transmitting, in any mode induced by vehicular impact.
Suicide prevention measures and vehicle parapets
4.70
Where the need for additional suicide prevention measures has been identified in the scheme suicide
review report, undertaken in accordance with GG 920 [Ref 72.N], suicide risk mitigation measures shall
be included as a design output.
4.70.1
At locations where vehicle containment is required, suicide risk mitigation measures may include:
1)
the installation of a vehicle parapet or a vehicle/pedestrian parapet with a minimum height of
1.8m and anti-climb features;
2)
increasing the height of an existing vehicle parapet or a vehicle/pedestrian parapet to a minimum
height of 1.8m and installing anti-climb features; or
3)
the installation of a pedestrian parapet which has a minimum height of 2.3m and anti-climb
features, with a separate safety barrier installed in front of it.
4.70.2
Anti-climb features should include a lack of toe or footholds.
NOTE
A foothold of 20 mm or greater is considered non-compliant with regard to 'anti-climb' conditions.
4.70.3
Anti-climb features may include the application of mesh to the front face of the pedestrian parapet and
or an inwardly sloping face.
4.70.4
Any pedestrian parapet installed as a suicide risk mitigation measure should be easier to scale from the
outside face in case an individual wishes to climb back to safety.
4.70.5
Where a separate safety barrier is installed in front of a pedestrian parapet, the barrier should be
positioned such that it does not aid climbing onto the pedestrian parapet.

4. Requirements for vehicle parapets
4.71
Where either a vehicle, vehicle/pedestrian or pedestrian parapet is proposed as a suicide risk
mitigation measure, wind loading calculations shall be carried out in accordance with CS 454 [Ref 3.N],
on a site-specific basis.
Reinforced concrete vehicle parapets
4.72
Vehicle parapets in concrete construction shall be specified in accordance with BS EN 1317-5 [Ref
54.N], unless they are bespoke for a particular structure.
NOTE
Bespoke vehicle parapets are those vehicle parapets which are only designed for one specific
location/structure, and therefore fall outside of the requirements of 2011/305/EU [Ref 8.N].
4.72.1
Bespoke vehicle parapets in concrete construction may be designed in accordance with BS 6779-2
1991 [Ref 36.N], as amended by Appendix E.
Stone or precast concrete copings on vehicle parapets
4.73
Stone or precast concrete copings shall only be used with vehicle parapets of concrete construction
where the permitted speed limit is 30 mph or less.
4.74
Stone and precast concrete copings shall be secured to the concrete backing by fixings capable of
resisting, at the ultimate limit state, a horizontal force of 33kN per metre of coping.
Masonry or brickwork facings on vehicle parapets
4.75
Masonry or brickwork facings shall only be provided after consultation with the responsible authorities
and with the prior agreement by the Overseeing Organisation.
4.76
Where reinforced concrete vehicle parapets are to be faced with masonry or brickwork, fixings shall be
provided between the concrete and facings, spaced at not more than 450mm horizontally and 300mm
vertically.
4.77
Where reinforced concrete vehicle parapets are to be faced with masonry or brickwork, brick reinforcing
mesh shall be incorporated into the bedding joints below those containing the fixings.
4.78
Where reinforced concrete vehicle parapets are to be faced with masonry or brickwork, fixings and
reinforcing mesh shall be stainless steel or hot dip galvanised reinforcement which meets the
requirements of BS EN 10348 [Ref 70.N].
4.79
Uncoursed masonry or brickwork shall only be used on a vehicle parapet where a risk assessment has
shown the risk to be SFAIRP.
4.80
Uncoursed masonry or brickwork shall not be used on the face of the vehicle parapet which is closest
to the carriageway.
4.81
Where reinforced concrete vehicle parapets are to be faced with masonry or brickwork, fixings and
reinforcing mesh shall not be placed in contact with carbon steel reinforcement.
4.82
Where reinforced concrete vehicle parapets are to be faced with masonry, the stone used shall be
close jointed ashlar or smooth blocks.
4.82.1
Masonry on the front face of the vehicle parapet may have an irregular surface finish, but overall, the
vehicle parapet is to be smooth faced.
4.82.2
Where masonry on the front face of the vehicle parapet has an irregular surface finish, the plane
through the peaks should be flat for straight vehicle parapets, and follow the nominal vehicle parapet
curvature for curved vehicle parapets.
4.83
Where reinforced concrete vehicle parapets are to be faced with brickwork, bricks shall have a smooth
surface.
4.84
Where reinforced concrete vehicle parapets are to be faced with brickwork, the pointing shall be near
flush.

4. Requirements for vehicle parapets
Masonry vehicle parapets
4.85
New and replacement masonry vehicle parapets shall not be installed except where agreed in advance
by the Overseeing Organisation.
4.86
New and replacement masonry vehicle parapets shall not be used on road bridges and structures over
or adjacent to railways except where agreed by the Overseeing Organisation and the Railway Authority.
4.87
The treatment of existing masonry vehicle parapet structures shall be agreed with the Overseeing
Organisation.
NOTE
Existing masonry vehicle parapets can have a number of faults and need to be examined and
assessed in accordance with the Department for Transport's guidance on the design, assessment and
strengthening of masonry vehicle parapets on highway structures in Masonry Parapets Guidance [Ref
30.N].
Aesthetic requirements for vehicle parapets
4.88
Drawings and specifications relating to the aesthetic requirements for the vehicle parapet shall be
agreed with the Overseeing Organisation.
4.89
Any specific aesthetic requirements for the vehicle parapet shall be given as a design output.

Requirements for vehicle/pedestrian parapets
General requirements for vehicle/pedestrian parapets
5.1
Vehicle/pedestrian parapets shall meet the requirements of Sections 4 and 9 of this document.
5.2
Where the requirements in Sections 4 and 9 of this document are different, the requirement which is
higher in rank, status, or quality shall apply.

6. Requirements for terminals
6.
Requirements for terminals
General requirements for terminals
6.1
Terminals shall be provided on the end(s) of a safety barrier to protect against a head-on vehicle impact.
6.2
Factors that limit the choice of terminal for a particular situation shall be included as a design output.
Performance class for terminals
6.3
On roads with a speed limit of 50 mph or more, terminals that face oncoming traffic shall have a
performance class of either T110 or T110/1 as defined by PD CEN/TS 1317-7 [Ref 60.N], or P4 as
defined by DD ENV 1317-4 2002 [Ref 45.N].
NOTE
On a two-way single carriageway road, the terminals on both ends of a safety barrier are examples of
terminals that face oncoming traffic.
6.4
On roads with a speed limit of 50 mph or more, terminals that do not face oncoming traffic shall have a
minimum performance class of T80/3 as defined by PD CEN/TS 1317-7 [Ref 60.N], or P1 as defined by
DD ENV 1317-4 2002 [Ref 45.N].
NOTE
Examples of terminals that do not face oncoming traffic include terminals on the trailing ends of safety
barriers on dual carriageway roads, terminals on the trailing end of a safety barrier on a one-way road,
or leading end terminals which are located behind a sufficient length of safety barrier.
6.5
On roads with a speed limit of less than 50 mph, terminals shall have a minimum performance class of
T80/3 as defined by PD CEN/TS 1317-7 [Ref 60.N], or P1 as defined by DD ENV 1317-4 2002 [Ref
45.N].
6.6
Terminal performance class shall be included as a design output for both the leading end and the trailing
end of each safety barrier, except for locations where the safety barrier transitions into another VRS.
Energy absorbing characteristic of terminals
6.7
On roads with a speed limit of 50 mph or more, leading terminals (that face oncoming traffic), shall be
energy absorbing.
NOTE 1
An example of terminals that face oncoming traffic are terminals on both ends of a safety barrier on a
two-way single carriageway road.
NOTE 2
On roads with a speed limit of less than 50 mph, terminals do not need to be energy absorbing.
6.8
The energy absorbing characteristic of a terminal shall be included as a design output for both the
leading end and the trailing end of each safety barrier, except for those locations where the safety
barrier transitions into another VRS or a structure.
Single and double sided terminals
6.9
Where a terminal is located in a position where it is only possible for it to be struck on one side, a single
sided terminal shall be included as a design output.
6.10
Where a terminal is located in a position where it is possible for it to be struck on either side, a double
sided terminal shall be included as a design output.
Direction of traffic past terminals
6.11
The direction of traffic past terminal value (one or two) shall be included as a design output.
6.12
A terminal located such that it is possible for it to be struck in only one direction shall have a direction of
traffic past terminal value of one.
6.12.1
A check should be made to ensure that the direction in which the terminal has been tested is the same
as the one direction in which it could be struck when installed.
68
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025



======================================================================
PAGE 70 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 Version 5.0.0
6. Requirements for terminals
NOTE
Examples of a terminal that can be struck in only one direction would be a terminal in the verge of a
motorway, on a slip road, at a nosing between two carriageways travelling in the same direction, or on a
one-way road.
6.13
Terminals located such that they could be struck in either direction shall have a direction of traffic past
terminal value of two.
NOTE
An example of a terminal that could be struck in either direction would be a terminal on a single
carriageway road where there is no central reserve.
Impact severity level (ISL) of terminals
6.14
The ISL for terminals shall be either ISL A or ISL B.
6.14.1
ISL A should be selected over ISL B as it affords a lower level of injury risk to the occupants of an
errant vehicle than ISL B.
Lateral displacement zone class of terminals
6.15
The maximum permissible lateral displacement zone classes for the terminal shall be given as design
outputs to ensure that it is not possible for any part of a deformed terminal to encroach into any hazard
or area used by road users, road workers and/or other parties in the event of an impact with the
terminal.
NOTE
PD CEN/TS 1317-7 [Ref 60.N] uses the term "permanent displacement zone" instead of "lateral
displacement zone".
6.16
Where the safety barrier is to be flared to maintain set-back to the end terminal, this shall be included in
the measurement of the available lateral displacement zone class.
6.17
Where the safety barrier is to be flared to maintain set-back to the end terminal, the space available for
the flare of the safety barrier and the set-back (to allow for the terminal) shall be given as a design
output.
Exit box class of terminals
6.18
For each installation, the maximum exit box class that the local hazard(s) allow, shall be given as a
design output.
NOTE
PD CEN/TS 1317-7 [Ref 60.N] uses the term "redirection zone" instead of "exit box class".
6.19
The exit box class for the terminal (Z1, Z2, Z3 or Z4) shall be given as a design output to ensure that it
is not possible for any redirected impacting vehicle to encroach into any hazard or area used by road
users, road workers and/or other parties, apart from being redirected back onto the hard
shoulder/carriageway which it had previously left.
6.19.1
Terminals with exit box classes Z3 and Z4 should only be used where there are no hazards on the
departure side of the terminal which have the potential to be reached by an errant vehicle.
NOTE
Errant vehicles might end up on the departure side of terminals with exit box classes Z3 and Z4.
6.19.2
Other VRS may be located within the exit box class for the terminal, but not in advance of the terminal.
6.20
No road furniture, including passively safe road furniture, shall be positioned less than 6 m in advance
of a new or existing terminal, apart from at a right of way through a continuous length of safety barrier
or at an ECP.
Locating two terminals close to each other
6.21
Where two terminals are to be located close to each other, the terminals shall be arranged such that
they are outside of each others lateral displacement zone class and exit box class and in such a way
that SFAIRP, it is not possible for for both terminals to be impacted simultaneously by the same errant
vehicle.
69
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

PAGE 71 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 Version 5.0.0
6. Requirements for terminals
NOTE
Locating terminals outside of each others lateral displacement zone class and exit box class could
mean that one terminal is located further downstream than the other terminal.
6.22
Where two terminals are to be located close to each other, the terminals shall be arranged such that the
risk of a vehicle(s) travelling between the two terminals is mitigated SFAIRP.
NOTE
Where two terminals are to be located close to each other, a double sided terminal is a preferable
solution where there is no difference in height between the two terminals.

7. Requirements for transitions
7.
Requirements for transitions
General requirements for transitions
7.1
A transition shall be included between two VRS where one or more of the following criteria apply:
1)
of different cross section;
2)
of different containment level;
3)
of different material;
4)
whose working width classes differ by more than one class; or
5)
whose vehicle intrusion classes differ by more than one class (for higher and very high
containment safety barriers and/or parapets).
7.2
A transition shall be included between a VRS and a structure, where the VRS and the structure are
connected.
7.3
The transition shall provide a smooth change in alignment and not allow the safety barrier or parapet to
become exposed to a head on impact.
7.3.1
The transition should provide a smooth change in height and not allow the safety barrier or parapet to
become exposed to a head on impact.
NOTE
The purpose of transitions is to provide a gradual change in performance from the first barrier to the
second, and to prevent the hazards of abrupt variations.
7.4
The vehicle restraint system(s) and/or structure on the leading and trailing end of the transition shall be
given as design outputs.
7.5
Transitions shall be compliant with BS EN 1317-1 [Ref 62.N], and either DD ENV 1317-4 2002 [Ref
45.N], or Assessment Method A1 or Assessment Method A2 in PD CEN/TR 1317-10 [Ref 58.N]unless
the connected VRS differ by one working width class or less, and have the same containment level,
and are manufactured from the same material.
7.6
Transitions between VRS which differ by one working width class or less, and have the same
containment level, and are manufactured from the same material, shall be compliant with Assessment
Method B1F or Assessment Level B2F in PD CEN/TR 1317-10 [Ref 58.N].
7.7
Proprietary transitions between two VRS to be connected shall be preferred to non proprietary
transitions.
7.7.1
Where proprietary transitions between two VRS to be connected are not available, the non proprietary
transitions detailed in NPSBS v1 2005 [Ref 42.N]should be used.
7.8
Where the design includes a requirement for an expansion joint, the design outputs for the expansion
joint shall be completed as for a transition.
7.9
Where the design includes a requirement for an expansion joint, the maximum longitudinal and/or
lateral movement shall be included as a design output.
Minimum containment levels of transitions
7.10
The containment level of a transition shall be the same as, or greater than, the lower containment level
of the two connected VRS.
NOTE
For example if an N2 containment safety barrier is connected to an H2 containment parapet, the
containment level of the connecting transition is to be N2 or greater.
Impact severity level (ISL) of transitions
7.11
The ISL of a transition shall not exceed ISL B unless the transition connects into
1)
an existing structure which has been categorised as Group 3 (low risk) according to CS 453 [Ref
75.N]; or
71
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025



======================================================================
PAGE 73 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 Version 5.0.0
7. Requirements for transitions
2)
a new structure which has been designed to resist main and residual loads according to BS EN
1991-1-7 [Ref 19.N].
7.11.1
ISL A should be selected over ISL B as it affords a lower level of injury risk to the occupants of an
errant vehicle than ISL B.
7.12
Where a transition connects into an existing structure which has been categorised as Group 3 (low risk)
according to CS 453 [Ref 75.N] or a new structure which has been designed to resist main and residual
loads according to BS EN 1991-1-7 [Ref 19.N], the ISL of the transition shall not exceed ISL C.
7.12.1
ISL B should be selected over ISL C as it affords a lower level of injury risk to the occupants of an
errant vehicle than ISL C.
Transitions and vehicle parapets
7.13
Where a new safety barrier is to be connected into an existing vehicle parapet or vehicle/pedestrian
parapet, the vehicle parapet or vehicle/pedestrian parapet shall be assessed in accordance with CS
461 [Ref 2.N] prior to the completion of the design.
7.14
Where a connection is required between a vehicle parapet and a transition, the vehicle parapet shall be
capable of providing the anchorage required by the transition and attached safety barrier in order for
the safety barrier and transition to achieve their full performance.
7.14.1
Changing a connection between an existing vehicle parapet and a transition may require the end
post(s) of an existing vehicle parapet to be modified.
NOTE
This modification can involve replacing a single large post with 2 smaller posts or can involve modifying
vehicle parapet post centres to receive the transition according to the manufacturer's installation
instructions.
Transitions between safety barriers not on a motorway or all-purpose trunk
road, and parapets over a motorway or all-purpose trunk road
7.15
Where a safety barrier not on a motorway or all-purpose trunk road connects to a vehicle parapet (via
transitions) on a bridge which crosses over a motorway or all-purpose trunk road, the design and
specification for the safety barriers and transitions shall be agreed between all parties to ensure that it
is possible to safely operate and maintain the full system.
7.15.1
Where a safety barrier not on a motorway or all-purpose trunk road connects to a vehicle parapet (via
transitions) on a bridge which crosses over a motorway or all-purpose trunk road, the safety barrier and
transitions should meet the requirements of this document.
NOTE
Guidance on the setting out of operational and maintenance boundaries where a safety barrier not on a
motorway or all-purpose trunk road connects to a parapet (via transitions) on a bridge which crosses
over a motorway or all-purpose trunk road, can be found in DoAMR [Ref 30.I].

8. Requirements for crash cushions
8.
Requirements for crash cushions
General requirements for crash cushions
8.1
Crash cushions shall be provided on the leading end of fixed and/or rigid objects which are not to be
removed, relocated or made passively safe, to reduce the risk of injury to vehicle occupants in the
event of an impact, where there is insufficient space to provide a compliant length of need of safety
barrier and terminal.
8.1.1
Crash cushions may be provided where:
1)
there is insufficient space to provide two single sided terminals;
2)
there is insufficient space to provide a double sided terminal; or
3)
it is not possible to install a safety barrier and terminal(s) in accordance with the manufacturer's
installation instructions.
NOTE
Fixed and/or rigid objects include roadside features such as bridge piers and toll booths.
Performance levels of crash cushions
8.2
For roads with a speed limit greater than 50 mph, the performance level of the crash cushion shall be
110, as defined by BS EN 1317-3 [Ref 44.N], and given as a design output.
8.3
For roads with a speed limit of 50 mph or less, the minimum performance level of the crash cushion
shall be 100, as defined by BS EN 1317-3 [Ref 44.N], and given as a design output.
Re-directive and non re-directive types of crash cushion
8.4
Where a risk assessment has identified that the redirection of an errant vehicle by a crash cushion
results in additional risk to the road user, road workers, or other parties, a non re-directive crash
cushion shall be included as a design output.
8.5
Where a risk assessment has identified that a crash cushion not redirecting an errant vehicle results in
additional risk to the road user, road workers, or other parties, a re-directive temporary crash cushion
shall be included as a design output.
Bi-directional and directional types of crash cushion
8.6
The type of crash cushion (bidirectional or directional) shall be included as a design output.
8.7
Crash cushions located such that they could be struck from either direction shall be bi-directional.
NOTE
An example of a crash cushion that could be struck in either direction would be a crash cushion on a
single carriageway road where there is no central reserve.
8.8
Crash cushions located such that they could be struck from one direction only shall be directional or
bi-directional.
NOTE
Examples of a crash cushion that can be struck in only one direction would be a crash cushion in the
verge of a motorway, on a slip road, at a nosing between two carriageways travelling in the same
direction, or on a one-way road.
8.9
Crash cushions shall be selected and positioned such that the direction in which the crash cushion has
been tested aligns with the direction it could be struck, when installed.
Impact severity level (ISL) of crash cushions
8.10
The ISL for crash cushions shall be either ISL A or ISL B.
8.10.1
ISL A should be selected over ISL B as it affords a lower level of injury risk to the occupants of an
errant vehicle than ISL B.
73
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025



======================================================================
PAGE 75 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 Version 5.0.0
8. Requirements for crash cushions
Vehicle redirection zone class of crash cushions
8.11
The vehicle redirection zone class for the crash cushion (Z1, Z2, Z3 or Z4) shall be given as a design
output to ensure that it is not possible for any redirected impacting vehicle to encroach into any hazard
or area used by road users, road workers and/or other parties, apart from being redirected back onto
the hard shoulder/carriageway which it had previously left.
8.11.1
Crash cushions with exit box classes Z3 and Z4 should only be used where there are no hazards on
the departure side of the crash cushion which have the potential to be reached by an errant vehicle.
NOTE
Errant vehicles might end up on the departure side of crash cushions with exit box classes Z3 and Z4.
8.12
Where a re-directive crash cushion has been given as a design output, the vehicle redirection zone
class shall be given to ensure that any redirected impacting vehicle does not encroach into any hazard
or area used by road users, road workers and/or other parties, apart from being redirected back onto
the carriageway which it had previously left.
8.12.1
Other VRS may be located within the exit box class for the crash cushion, but not in advance of the
crash cushion.
8.13
No road furniture, including passively safe road furniture, shall be positioned less than 6 m in advance
of a new or existing crash cushion.
Permanent lateral displacement zone class of crash cushions
8.14
The permanent lateral displacement zone class for the crash cushion (D1 to D8) shall be given as a
design output to ensure that no part of the deformed crash cushion encroaches into any hazard or area
used by road users, road workers and/or other parties.

9. Requirements for pedestrian restraint systems
9.
Requirements for pedestrian restraint systems
General requirements for pedestrian restraint systems
9.1
The requirements of this section shall apply to all roads within the scope of the Overseeing
Organisation.
9.2
Pedestrian restraint systems shall be provided where a risk assessment has identified a risk of injury
from a fall from a height, and or a risk of injury from entering a dangerous area.
NOTE 1
LTN 2/09 [Ref 46.I] provides an acceptable approach for the risk assessment for pedestrian guardrails.
NOTE 2
CD 143 [Ref 17.N] provides requirements and advice for designing for walking, cycling and horse-riding.
NOTE 3
GG 142 [Ref 55.I] provides requirements for walking, cycling and horse-riding assessments.
NOTE 4
Typical locations for a pedestrian restraint system are shown in Figure 9.2N4.

9. Requirements for pedestrian restraint systems
9.2.1
The risk assessment which has identified a risk of injury from a fall from a height, or a risk of injury from
entering a dangerous area, should also include the additional risk to vehicle occupants due to the
introduction of the pedestrian restraint system, if the pedestrian restraint system could be reached by a
vehicle.
9.3
Where the pedestrian restraint system is located such that it could be reached by a vehicle, the design
of the pedestrian restraint system shall be such that the risk of the pedestrian restraint system
becoming disconnected or breaking on impact in such a way as to cause a hazard to users of the WCH
route, other road users, road workers, or other parties, is SFAIRP.
NOTE
A pedestrian restraint system is not required to perform as a vehicle restraint system, but the
pedestrian restraint system can be located in a position where it could still be reached, and impacted,
by an errant vehicle.
9.4
The minimum dimensions for the set-back of a pedestrian restraint system shall be as shown in Table
9.4.
Table 9.4 Minimum set-back of pedestrian restraint systems
Speed limit of road
Minimum set-back of pedestrian restraint system (mm)
Less than 50 mph
450
50 mph
600
Greater than 50 mph
1000
9.5
The set-back shall be the lateral distance between the traffic face of a pedestrian restraint system and:
1)
nearside: the back of the nearside hard strip or hard shoulder;
2)
nearside: the kerb face for roads without a nearside hard strip or hard shoulder;
3)
offside: the trafficked edge of the edge line;
4)
offside: the kerb face where there is no edge line.
9.6
For roads with a speed limit of 50mph or more, all pedestrian restraint systems shall be installed
outside the normalised working width and, for higher or very high containment vehicle restraint
systems, the normalised vehicle intrusion of a safety barrier that is required for other reasons.
9.7
The class of nominal live loads for the posts and rails of the pedestrian restraint system shall be given
as a design output.
NOTE
Further details of the classes of nominal live loads for the posts and rails of the pedestrian restraint
system are given in BS 7818 [Ref 68.N].
9.8
The class of nominal loads for the bar, sheet or mesh infill of the pedestrian restraint system shall be
given as a design output.
NOTE
Further details of the classes of nominal loads for the bar, sheet or mesh infill of the pedestrian restraint
system are given in BS 7818 [Ref 68.N].
9.9
The minimum height of the pedestrian restraint system shall be given as a design output.
9.10
Any specific aesthetic requirements for the pedestrian restraint system shall be given as a design
output.
9.11
When designing the vertical infill bar components for a pedestrian restraint system, all of the loading at
700 mm centres in Clause 2.1.4.3 of BS 7818 [Ref 68.N] shall be applied simultaneously, and not
individually.
General requirements for all pedestrian parapets
9.12
At locations where a pedestrian parapet is proposed, an assessment of wind actions on the pedestrian
parapet shall be undertaken in accordance with BS EN 1991-1-4 [Ref 23.N] and NA to BS EN 1991-1-4
[Ref 89.N], on a site-specific basis.

9. Requirements for pedestrian restraint systems
9.13
At locations where a pedestrian parapet is installed, the risk of fatigue damage due to vortex excitation
shall be investigated in accordance with CD 363 [Ref 16.N].
9.14
When it is necessary to increase the height of an existing pedestrian parapet, any extension shall be
compatible with, and not be detrimental to, the performance of the pedestrian parapet system to which
it is attached.
9.14.1
The additional height may be provided by the use of an additional structural extension to the pedestrian
parapet.
9.15
Where a structural extension is added to an existing pedestrian parapet, the addition of the structural
extension shall be confirmed as acceptable by the manufacturer/promoter of the pedestrian parapet
system, where the manufacturer/promoter of the system still exists.
9.16
Where a structural extension is added to an existing pedestrian parapet, the addition of the structural
extension shall be confirmed as acceptable by the Overseeing Organisation, where the
manufacturer/promoter of the pedestrian parapet system no longer exists.
9.16.1
Where repair parts are available and the increased height variant of the pedestrian parapet exists, the
change in height should be achieved by the exchange of standard parts compliant with the original
manufacturer's specification.
9.17
Where the height of an existing pedestrian parapet is to be increased, the effect of any additional
loading on the supporting structure as a result of this modification, shall be assessed and remedial
measures undertaken, where necessary.
Additional requirements for all pedestrian parapets over or adjacent to railways
9.18
Pedestrian parapets over railways shall have solid infilling to their full height.
9.19
Infill panels on the front face of a pedestrian parapets shall be of a design and material approved by the
Railway Authority.
9.20
No toeholds shall be provided on the front face of the pedestrian parapet or the infill panel.
General requirements for all pedestrian guardrails
9.21
Pedestrian guardrails shall be of metal construction.
General requirements for pedestrian restraint systems located adjacent to WCH
routes
9.22
Where a structure on a WCH route presents a vertical or near vertical face 1.5 m or more in height and
it is possible to gain access to the upper edge of the structure, a pedestrian parapet shall be installed
close to, or on top of, the unprotected edge of the structure.
9.23
Where a structure on a WCH route presents a vertical or near vertical face less than 1.5 m in height
and it is possible to gain access to the upper edge of the structure, a pedestrian parapet or pedestrian
guardrail shall be installed close to, or on top of, the unprotected edge of the structure if a risk of injury
has been identified through a risk assessment.
9.23.1
A risk of injury may result from the presence of a road, railway or watercourse under or adjacent to the
structure.
9.24
Where a metal pedestrian restraint system is located adjacent to a WCH route, the pedestrian restraint
system shall meet the requirements of BS 7818 [Ref 68.N] and CG 300 [Ref 73.N].
9.25
Where a clause within BS 7818 [Ref 68.N] makes reference to a standard which has now been
superseded, the requirements of the most recent standard shall be used.
9.26
Where a metal pedestrian restraint system is located adjacent to a WCH route, the pedestrian restraint
system shall be of framed construction consisting of posts and longitudinal members with infilling.

9. Requirements for pedestrian restraint systems
Requirements for pedestrian parapets located adjacent to WCH routes
9.27
All non vehicular bridges with a WCH route shall be provided with pedestrian parapets.
9.28
Where a metal pedestrian parapet is located adjacent to a WCH route, the posts and rails shall meet
the Class 3 nominal live loads in BS 7818 [Ref 68.N], unless this is deemed to be inadequate by a risk
assessment.
9.29
Where the Class 3 nominal live loads for posts and rails are assessed by risk assessment to be
inadequate, Class 4 nominal live loads for posts and rails shall be used, depending on the outcome of
the risk assessment.
9.30
Where a metal pedestrian parapet is located adjacent to a WCH route, the bar, sheet or mesh infill shall
meet the Class C nominal loads in BS 7818 [Ref 68.N], unless this is deemed to be inadequate by a
risk assessment.
9.31
Where the Class C nominal loads for the bar, sheet or mesh infill are assessed by risk assessment to
be inadequate, Class D nominal loads for the bar, sheet or mesh infill infill shall be used.
9.32
The minimum height of a new pedestrian parapet adjacent to a walking route shall be 1150 mm, unless
the WCH route goes over or is adjacent to a railway.
9.33
The minimum height of a new pedestrian parapet adjacent to a cyclist route shall be 1400 mm, unless
the WCH goes over or is adjacent to a railway.
9.34
The minimum height of a new pedestrian parapet adjacent to a horse-riding route shall be 1800 mm.
9.35
The minimum height of a new pedestrian parapet adjacent to a WCH route which goes over or adjacent
to a railway shall be 1800 mm.
9.36
Where a bridge has provision for more than one user group, the taller height requirement shall apply to
the minimum height of the pedestrian parapet.
9.37
Where there is a horse-riding route adjacent to the pedestrian parapet which crosses or is adjacent to
another road, a minimum height of 600mm, when measured above the adjoining paved surface, shall
have a solid infill.
NOTE
The solid infill could be a combination of concrete plinth depth, infill panel and longitudinal parapet
elements.
9.38
Pedestrian parapets adjacent to a WCH route shall be mounted on a continuous plinth or continuous
upstand of 50 mm height with a tolerance of -0/+50 mm above the adjoining paved surface.
9.39
The design output shall identify where the parapet does not have a continuous plinth or continuous
upstand of 50mm height with a tolerance of -0/+50 mm above the adjoining paved surface.
9.40
Pedestrian parapets of solid construction shall be designed to resist the more severe of the nominal live
load in Table 9.40 applied transversely at the level of the top of the pedestrian parapet, or wind loading
in accordance with BS EN 1991-1-4 [Ref 23.N] and the NA to BS EN 1991-1-4 [Ref 89.N].
Table 9.40 Nominal live loads for pedestrian parapets of solid construction
Location type
Nominal live load (in kN/m)
Alongside a WCH route
1.5
Alongside a potentially crowded public area
3
NOTE
A potentially crowded public area might include a location close to a large sports or entertainment
venue.
9.40.1
With reference to BS 7818 [Ref 68.N] and BS EN 1992-2 [Ref 24.N], a partial load factor of 1.5 should
be taken for live load at the ultimate limit state, 1.4 for wind load at the ultimate limit state, or 1.0 for
both at the serviceability limit state.

9.40.2
The strength of infilling panels for a prototype design should be proved by test loading with the loads
situated in the most adverse positions, and where the minimum overload factor should be taken as
equal to the product of the partial safety factors used for ultimate limit state design.
9.40.3
When the appropriate design document given in the technical approval schedule is not to limit state
format, a 50% overload should be assumed.
9.41
Where a concrete pedestrian parapet is located adjacent to a WCH route, the pedestrian restraint
system shall meet the requirements of BS EN 1992-2 [Ref 24.N].
9.42
Bespoke pedestrian parapets manufactured from concrete shall conform to the requirements of the
loading described in Category C5 in Table 6.12 of BS EN 1991-1-1 [Ref 20.N] and Table NA.8 of BS EN
1991-1-1 [Ref 20.N].
9.43
Stone or precast copings used with concrete pedestrian parapets shall be secured to the concrete
backing by fixings capable or resisting at the ultimate limit state a design horizontal force of 33 kN per
metre of coping.
Requirements for pedestrian guardrails located adjacent to WCH routes
9.44
Where a metal pedestrian guardrail is located adjacent to a WCH route, the posts and rails shall meet
the Class 2 nominal live loads in BS 7818 [Ref 68.N], unless this is deemed to be inadequate by a risk
assessment.
9.45
Where the Class 2 nominal live loads for posts and rails are assessed by risk assessment to be
inadequate, Class 3 or 4 nominal live loads for posts and rails shall be used, depending on the
outcome of the risk assessment.
9.46
Where a metal pedestrian guardrail is located adjacent to a WCH route, the bar, sheet or mesh infill
shall meet the Class B nominal loads in BS 7818 [Ref 68.N], unless this is deemed to be inadequate by
a risk assessment.
9.47
Where the Class B nominal loads for the bar, sheet or mesh infill are assessed by risk assessment to
be inadequate, Class D nominal loads for the bar, sheet or mesh infill shall be used, depending on the
outcome of the risk assessment.
9.48
The minimum height of a new pedestrian guardrail adjacent to a walking or cycling route shall be 1000
mm.
9.49
The minimum height of a new pedestrian guardrail adjacent to a horse-riding route shall be 1800 mm.
9.50
Pedestrian guardrails shall not be provided as a deterrent to kerbside vehicle parking.
General requirements for pedestrian restraint systems not located adjacent to
WCH routes
9.51
Where a structure not on a WCH route presents a vertical or near vertical face 1.5 m or more in height
and it is possible to gain access to the upper edge of the structure, a pedestrian parapet or pedestrian
guardrail shall be installed close to, or on top of, the unprotected edge of the structure if a risk of injury
has been identified through a risk assessment, unless the structure goes over or is adjacent to a railway,
NOTE 1
Drivers and passengers of broken down or damaged vehicles, maintenance staff, emergency service
personnel and others might, on occasion, need to walk close to pedestrian restraint systems which are
not located adjacent to WCH routes, and there is still a potential risk of persons falling from the top of
the wall or structure, particularly in poor visibility or adverse weather conditions.
NOTE 2
Requirements for pedestrian restraint systems located adjacent to access steps at technology sites can
be found in MCX 0138 1992 [Ref 87.N].
9.51.1
A risk of injury may include the presence of a road, railway or watercourse in close proximity to the
structure.
9.52
Where a structure not on a WCH route over or adjacent to a railway presents a vertical or near vertical
face 1.5 m or more in height and it is possible to gain access to the upper edge of the structure, a
pedestrian parapet shall be installed close to, or on top of, the unprotected edge of the structure.
