CD 377 - ENAA Version 1.0.0
E/1. Scope (additional to CD 377)
E/1.
Scope (additional to CD 377)
Definition of Overseeing Organisation
E/1.1
Where the core CD 377 [Ref 12.N] are this English National Application Annex are to be used for
National Highways roads (or their successors), the term 'Overseeing Organisation' shall be read as
'VRS Champion or Safety, Engineering and Standards (SES) VRS Adviser'.
Implementation and application (CD 377, 1)
Unprotected hazards on motorways and all-purpose trunk roads with a maximum speed limit of
50 mph or more, and two-way traffic flow of 5,000 annual average daily traffic (AADT) or more
E/1.2
Where RRS works (except routine maintenance and safety critical interventions) are proposed on
motorways and all-purpose trunk roads with a maximum speed limit of 50 mph or more, and two-way
traffic flow of 5,000 annual average daily traffic (AADT) or more, and within 100 m of unprotected
hazards in the same verge or central reserve, mitigation of the unprotected hazards shall be included
within the works, unless agreed otherwise in advance with the VRS Champion or SES VRS Adviser,
and supported by a GG 104 [Ref 13.N] risk assessment.
E/1.2.1
If further unprotected hazards are then identified within 100 m of the extended RRS works, mitigation of
the additional unprotected hazards may be excluded from the works, with the prior agreement of the
VRS Champion or SES VRS Adviser, and where supported by a GG 104 [Ref 13.N] risk assessment.
NOTE
This is aimed at balancing the reduction of risk posed by nearby hazards, whilst avoiding extensive
increases in scope.
E/1.3
Any identified unprotected hazards shall be reported to the VRS Champion for addition to a list of future
RRS needs.
NOTE
The list of future RRS needs is typically held by the VRS Champion.
Like-for-like renewal (additional to CD 377, 1.4.1)
E/1.4
Where an existing RRS requires a safety critical intervention, a like-for-like renewal of a RRS shall be
agreed with the VRS Champion or an SES VRS Adviser prior to incorporation into the design.
9
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

E/2. General requirements (additional to CD 377)
E/2.
General requirements (additional to CD 377)
General requirements for risk assessments for road restraint systems (CD 377,
2)
E/2.1
Except where reference to the RRRAP [Ref 20.N] or tRRRAP is made within CD 377 [Ref 12.N], any
other reference within CD 377 [Ref 12.N] to a "risk assessment" shall be read as a "risk assessment
complying with the requirements of GG 104 [Ref 13.N]".
General design requirements for road restraint systems (CD 377, 2.57)
Additional requirements for RRS
E/2.2
For non-harmonised products, the design of the RRS shall take into account any restriction(s) on the
product(s) which is stated within the product's letter of acceptance.

CD 377 - ENAA Version 1.0.0
E/3. Requirements for permanent safety barriers (a...
E/3.
Requirements for permanent safety barriers (additional to CD 377)
Gaps between lengths of safety barrier (CD 377, 3.34-3.37)
E/3.1
The closure of a gap of up to 100 m in length on a motorway with no hardshoulder, shall be subject to a
risk assessment.
E/3.1.1
A risk assessment associated with the closure of a gap within a motorway with no hardshoulder should
include the following:
1)
the length of gap achievable;
2)
the relative set back of adjacent sections of VRS;
3)
the verge width;
4)
the ground conditions of the verge and the estimated level of difficulty in getting vehicle on and
back off the verge;
5)
whether vehicles able to get fully off the carriageway/hardstrip;
6)
whether the rear of a stranded vehicle is a risk to following traffic;
7)
sightline and stopping sight distance in advance of the gap;
8)
sightline and stopping sight distance in advance of the stranded vehicle;
9)
the safety of passengers exiting stranded vehicles;
10)
the presence of hazardous features in and beyond the verge for which VRS is not warranted, but
which pose a hazard for occupants of a stranded vehicle;
11)
the provision of lighting;
12)
the proximity to an emergency area, if applicable, and the risks involved in reaching it it;
13)
the location of the gap relative to sign gantries and cameras and the visibility of the location from
cameras;
14)
maintenance needs including access requirements; and
15)
significant cost, technical or other access requirements for the gap to remain open.
E/3.2
Where a gap is not closed due to significant cost, technical or access requirements, the reasons for the
decision shall be recorded in the Heath and Safety file for the scheme.
Motorcyclist protection devices (CD 377, 3.42)
E/3.3
Where an increased level of injury risk due to loss of control to motorcyclists is identified, appropriate
mitigation measures compliant with PD CEN/TS 17342 [Ref 14.N] shall be included as a design output,
subject to a risk assessment.
NOTE
Further guidance for designing for motorcyclists can be found in NH GDM [Ref 1.I].
Safety barrier provision in central reserves - general (CD 377, 3.79)
Safety barrier provision in central reserves of new roads
E/3.4
On new motorways with a predicted two-way annual average daily traffic (AADT) greater than or equal
to 25,000 vehicles/day, where a safety barrier is required in accordance with CD 377 [Ref 12.N], and
the distance Psb to Psb is 10 metres or less, and the length of safety barrier to be installed is greater
than 500 m, a rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50 years and a minimum
containment level of H1 shall be installed in the central reserve.
NOTE
The installation of a safety barrier with a minimum containment level of H1 is to reduce the risk of
cross-over incidents.
E/3.4.1
Where the length of safety barrier to be installed in the central reserve of a new motorway is 500 m or
less, a non rigid safety barrier with a minimum containment level of N2 may be installed instead.
11
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

PAGE 141 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 - ENAA Version 1.0.0
E/3. Requirements for permanent safety barriers (a...
E/3.5
Where a road is being designed as an enhanced all-purpose dual carriageway in accordance with GD
300 [Ref 11.N], the requirements of GD 300 [Ref 11.N] shall apply.
E/3.6
Where a safety barrier is required in the central reserve of a new road in accordance with CD 377 [Ref
12.N], and the distance Psb to Psb is 10 m or less, and the road is not a motorway with a two-way
annual average daily traffic (AADT) greater than or equal to 25,000 vehicles/day or an enhanced
all-purpose dual carriageway, a risk assessment shall be carried out to determine whether it is
appropriate to increase the containment in the central reserve above the minimum containment level of
N2.
E/3.7
Factors to incorporate into a risk assessment carried out to determine whether it is appropriate to
increase the containment above the minimum containment level of N2 shall include:
1)
the AADT of the road;
2)
the number of HGVs using the road;
3)
the number of cross-over incidents;
4)
the number of repairs to the central reserve safety barrier; and
5)
any other factors increasing the risk of an impact with the safety barrier in the central reserve.
NOTE
An example of a factor which increases the risk of an impact with the safety barrier in the central
reserve is a flooding hot spot.
Safety barrier provision in central reserves of existing roads
E/3.8
On existing motorways with a two-way annual average daily traffic (AADT) greater than or equal to
25,000 vehicles/day, where a safety barrier is required in accordance with CD 377 [Ref 12.N], the
distance Psb to Psb is 10 metres or less, and the length of safety barrier to be installed is greater than
500 m, the safety barrier in the central reserve shall have a minimum containment level of H1.
NOTE
The installation of a safety barrier with a minimum containment level of H1 is to reduce the risk of
cross-over incidents.
E/3.8.1
Where the length of safety barrier to be installed in the central reserve of an existing motorway is 500 m
or less, a non rigid safety barrier with a minimum containment level of N2 may be installed instead.
E/3.8.2
On existing motorways with a two-way AADT greater than or equal to 25,000 vehicles/day, where a
safety barrier greater than 500 m in length is required in accordance with CD 377 [Ref 12.N], and the
distance Psb to Psb is 10 m or less, a rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50
years should be installed in the central reserve.
NOTE
The installation of a rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50 years is to reduce the
need for safety barriers to be repaired following an impact by an errant vehicle and hence, minimise the
congestion arising from temporary traffic management and reduce the risk to maintenance workers.
E/3.8.3
Subject to a GG 104 [Ref 13.N] risk assessment, a non-rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not
less than 50 years, should be installed in the central reserve where, due to current funding levels
and/or due to technical constraints and/or geometric constraints, it is not possible to install a rigid safety
barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50 years, subject to a GG 104 [Ref 13.N] risk assessment.
NOTE
Examples of technical constraints why a rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50
years cannot be installed include the availability of products with the required essential characteristics,
the inability of a structure to support the mass of the safety barrier, the lack of availability of transitions
to/from the barrier, the minimum installation length of the safety barrier, the depth and (typically)
continuous nature of the foundations for the barrier and/or the carbon cost of the product.
E/3.9
Where a non-rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50 years is to be installed in the
central reserve instead of a rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50 years, the
reason(s) for not installing a rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50 years, shall be
recorded.
12
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

CD 377 - ENAA Version 1.0.0
E/3. Requirements for permanent safety barriers (a...
E/3.9.1
Subject to a GG 104 [Ref 13.N] risk assessment, a non-rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of less
than 50 years, should be installed in the central reserve where, due to current funding levels and/or due
to technical constraints and/or geometric constraints, it is not possible to install a non-rigid safety
barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50 years.
NOTE
Examples of technical constraints why a non-rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than
50 years cannot be installed include the availability of products with the required essential
characteristics, the inability of a structure to support the mass of the safety barrier, the lack of
availability of transitions to/from the barrier, the minimum installation length of the safety barrier, the
foundation requirements for the barrier and/or the carbon cost of the product.
E/3.10
Where a non-rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of less than 50 years is to be installed in the
central reserve instead of a non-rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50 years, the
reason(s) for not installing a non-rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50 years,
shall be recorded.
E/3.11
Where a safety barrier is required in the central reserve of an exisiting road in accordance with CD 377
[Ref 12.N], and the distance Psb to Psb is 10 m or less, and the road is not a motorway with a two-way
annual average daily traffic (AADT) greater than or equal to 25,000 vehicles/day or an enhanced
all-purpose dual carriageway, a risk assessment shall be carried out to determine whether it is
appropriate to increase the containment in the central reserve above the minimum containment level of
N2.
E/3.12
Factors to incorporate into a risk assessment carried out to determine whether it is appropriate to
increase the containment above the minimum containment level of N2 shall include:
1)
the AADT of the road;
2)
the number of HGVs using the road;
3)
the number of cross-over incidents;
4)
the number of repairs to the central reserve safety barrier; and
5)
any other factors increasing the risk of an impact with the safety barrier in the central reserve.
NOTE
An example of a factor which increases the risk of an impact with the safety barrier in the central
reserve is a flooding hot spot.
The use of full height anchorages (FHA) at emergency areas (EA) on motorways
(CD 377, 3)
E/3.13
FHAs shall only be used at EA locations where they are positioned behind another VRS, and outside of
its normalised working width and vehicle intrusion.
E/3.14
The connection of a safety barrier to a FHA shall meet the requirements of a transition according to
Section 7 of CD 377 [Ref 12.N].
E/3.15
Unless specified otherwise by the safety barrier manufacturer, where two lengths of safety barrier are to
overlap, the safety barrier overlap at full height shall be a minimum of 10 m in length, excluding the
lengths of the FHAs.
E/3.16
Where the offset between two lengths of safety barrier is used to accommodate a maintenance area,
the length of safety barrier closest to the carriageway in advance of the maintenance area, shall meet
the requirements of Clauses 3.24 to 3.31 of CD 377 [Ref 12.N].
Entry slip signal sites (CD 377,3)
E/3.17
For post-mounted entry slip signal (ESS) sites, a lack of protection by a VRS, or the lack of provision of
the required approach length of safety barrier, shall be permitted as acceptable.
E/3.18
Each ESS site shall be risk assessed in accordance with GG 104 [Ref 13.N], and the decision as to
whether to provide VRS, the length of VRS, and the decision making process, recorded in the design
strategy record.
13

E/4. Requirements for vehicle parapets (additional...
E/4.
Requirements for vehicle parapets (additional to CD 377)
Design and assessment requirements for vehicle parapets and supporting
structures (CD 377, 4.60)
E/4.1
Any need to modify a bridge or structure to accommodate a UKCA/CE marked parapet shall be
discussed with the Structures Technical Approval Authority (TAA) at the earliest opportunity to agree a
way forward.
NOTE
Where the design incorporates the installation of a safety barrier between an existing parapet and the
edge of the carriageway instead of the renewal of an existing vehicle parapet, or the replacement of an
existing pedestrian parapet with a vehicle parapet, guidance on two possible unreinforced concrete
verge arrangements which can be included in the design can be found in Appendix E/B.
E/4.2
Any proposal to install surface-mounted barriers on unreinforced concrete verges on bridges shall be
discussed with the Structures TAA at the earliest opportunity to agree a way forward.

CD 377 - ENAA Version 1.0.0
E/5. Requirements for terminals (additional to CD ...
E/5.
Requirements for terminals (additional to CD 377)
Performance class for terminals (CD 377, 6.3-6.6)
E/5.1
Where an existing P1 terminal which faces oncoming traffic on a road with a speed limit of 50 mph or
greater and a two-way traffic flow of 5,000 or greater is to be renewed or replaced, the terminal shall be
replaced with a terminal with a performance class of T110 or T110/1 as defined by PD CEN/TS 1317-7
[Ref 15.N], or P4 as defined by DD ENV 1317-4 2002 [Ref 7.N].
E/5.1.1
The terminal may be replaced without renewal of the attached safety barrier provided that:
1)
the existing safety barrier to which the terminal is to be connected is in a satisfactory condition;
2)
where the existing safety barrier is a legacy system, the requirements in Table 12.8 of CD 377
[Ref 12.N] are met;
3)
the replacement terminal is capable of providing any anchorage which is required by the safety
barrier; and
4)
the VRS Champion or SES VRS Adviser, and the manufacturer of the terminal and any
proprietary safety barrier, have agreed to the change.
E/5.1.2
Where an existing P1 terminal which faces oncoming traffic on a road with a speed limit of 50 mph or
greater and an AADT of 5,000 or greater is to be repaired or replaced following incident damage, the
terminal may be replaced on a like-for-like basis unless it is a welded angle beam terminal.
15
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

======================================================================
CD 377 - ENAA Version 1.0.0
E/6. Requirements for pedestrian restraint systems...
E/6.
Requirements for pedestrian restraint systems (additional to CD
377)
Pedestrian restraint systems located at EAs (CD 377, 9)
E/6.1
Where a metal pedestrian restraint system is located at an EA, the design of the pedestrian restraint
system shall include features to reduce the risk of drivers and passengers of broken down or damaged
vehicles, maintenance staff, emergency service personnel getting underneath or through the
pedestrian restraint system.
NOTE
Features to reduce the risk of drivers and passengers of broken down or damaged vehicles,
maintenance staff, emergency service personnel getting underneath or through the pedestrian restraint
system can be provided by the addition of mesh and/or a bottom rail.
Pedestrian restraint systems at the top of embankments at EAs
E/6.2
Pedestrian restraint systems shall be provided at the top of embankments at EAs with
1)
a height of 0.5 m or greater; and
2)
a gradient steeper than 1 in 2.
E/6.3
Pedestrian restraint systems at the top of embankments at EAs shall meet the Class 2 nominal live
loads in BS 7818 [Ref 18.N].
E/6.4
Where the Class 2 nominal live loads for posts and rails are assessed by risk assessment to be
inadequate, a higher class of nominal live loads for posts and rails shall be used, depending on the
outcome of the risk assessment.
Pedestrian restraint systems on the top of retaining walls located at the top of an embankment
at EAs
E/6.5
Where a retaining wall greater than 0.5 m in height is located at the top of an embankment at an EA, a
pedestrian restraint system shall be provided on the top of the retaining wall.
E/6.6
Pedestrian restraint systems on the top of retaining walls shall meet the Class 2 nominal live loads in
BS 7818 [Ref 18.N].
E/6.7
Where the Class 2 nominal live loads for posts and rails are assessed by risk assessment to be
inadequate, a higher class of nominal live loads for posts and rails shall be used, depending on the
outcome of the risk assessment.
Edge protection on the top of retaining walls located at the bottom of an embankment at EAs
E/6.8
Where a retaining wall greater than 0.5 m in height is located at the bottom of an embankment at an
EA, edge protection shall be provided on the top of a retaining wall.
NOTE
A motorway and accommodation works timber post and 4 rail fence as detailed in LC 127 [Ref 2.N]
could be provided as edge protection.
16
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

E/7. Legacy systems (additional to CD 377)
E/7.
Legacy systems (additional to CD 377)
Connecting new VRS to an existing legacy system (CD 377, 12.7)
E/7.1
Where a new VRS is being connected to an existing legacy system, the existing legacy system shall be
in a satisfactory condition.

Appendix E/A. Process for the appointment of independent re...
Appendix E/A. Process for the appointment of independent reviewers (for
letters of acceptance for non-harmonised products)
E/A1
Competency requirements for independent reviewers (for letters of acceptance
for non-harmonised products)
Any organisation applying to National Highways for appointment as a reviewer for one or more
non-harmonised product types, will meet the following criteria:
1)
Be a UK approved body accredited for the assessment of BS EN 1317-5 [Ref 10.N] products,
and/or
2)
Be an organisation which can provide evidence that it complies with all of the following
requirements:
a)
is established under UK law and has legal personality;
b)
holds adequate public liability and professional indemnity insurance for the scope of the
review activities they wish to carry out, or this is fully held by the product
manufacturer/distributor/owner being reviewed by the independent reviewer;
c)
supplies evidence which demonstrates high levels of impartiality and independence;
d)
has a minimum of ten years' experience in the vehicle restraint systems sector;
e)
has a current working knowledge and experience of full scale impact testing for the
standards/requirements relevant to the products for which they are seeking appointment;
f)
has a working understanding of relevant National Highways Sector Schemes (NHSS);
g)
is able to demonstrate that it holds full responsibility for the contracts, activities and
decisions that it undertakes/makes;
h)
takes full responsibility for the performance and outcome of its review activities, i.e. have
full operational control over these activities. To this end, the organisation has appropriate
technical competence and the resources to assure control over the full scope of their
associated activities, and to take full responsibility for the competence and resources used,
the rules and procedures applied, the consistency obtained, and quality achieved through
the application of these rules and procedures, the impartiality displayed applying these
rules and procedures, and the contents of issued letters of acceptance;
i)
owns and operates an effective management system that clearly covers the activities of the
review activities;
j)
ensures all documents, policies and procedures are available in English;
k)
identifies the employees responsible for the product acceptance review activities;
l)
holds descriptions of the responsibilities and relevant authorisations of persons approving
policies and instructions for review activities, approving authorities and responsibilities of
personnel involved in product acceptance review activities, and authorising letters of
acceptance;
m) holds and stores all information received as a part of these activities in a secure manner,
and treats all information received in a confidential manner; and
n)
issues letters of acceptance using only the templates issued by National Highways.
Note: "established under UK law" means that the organisation is to be a registered UK legal entity (via
Companies House, or equivalent) with a registered UK address.
Evidence on each aspect should be submitted from the applicant to an SES VRS Adviser.
E/A2
Application process for independent reviewers (for letters of acceptance for
non-harmonised products)
The applicant should clearly identify within their application, which of the non-harmonised product
type(s) they are applying to review, on behalf of National Highways.
On receipt of an application, an SES VRS Adviser will review the application against the requirements
set out within the list of competency requirements for independent reviewers.
20
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

product type(s) has been received, and approved by National Highways (by letter).

CD 377 - ENAA Version 1.0.0
Appendix E/B. Installation of surface-mounted N1/N2 safety ...
Appendix E/B. Installation of surface-mounted N1/N2 safety barriers on
unreinforced concrete verges over bridges
E/B1
Introduction and background
This appendix provides design guidance in relation to simplified and cost-effective foundation slabs for
normal containment safety barriers in front of substandard bridge parapets which either require
replacing or protecting, or where protection is already in place but will need to be replaced sometime in
the future (normally when the bridge is to be waterproofed or when the existing safety barriers come to
the end of their useful working life).
Currently there is no specific design guidance in standards for the anchorage of surface mounted posts
for normal containment safety barrier posts on unreinforced, mass concrete verges or central reserves
overlying the structural deck at bridge locations.
The design guidance is based on full scale impact testing carried out in accordance with BS EN 1317-1
[Ref 17.N] and BS EN 1317-2 [Ref 16.N].
This new design guidance is intended to deliver benefits in terms of cost, applicability and reduced site
construction time, thereby reducing health and safety risk/exposure to the workforce and road user.
On bridges with a speed limit greater than 50 mph and with no hard shoulder or hard strip, and where
this system is not included in the barrier manufacturer's installation manual, this design guidance
should only be used with the prior approval of an SES VRS Adviser.
Two arrangements have been provided as design guidance below, and the choice between them, and
whether to use the arrangement at all, will depend upon the specific site conditions where the
arrangement is to be incorporated into the design.
E/B2
Simplified design guidance - arrangement 1
Existing and new unreinforced (mass) concrete verges and central reserves are to be deemed
adequate for the installation of surface mounted posts for normal containment safety barriers, subject
to the following design guidance being satisfied:
E/B2.1
Minimum verge/central reserve mass concrete dimensions - arrangement 1
Minimum verge/central reserve mass concrete dimensions (as illustrated in Figure E/B.1):
1)
Minimum length of mass concrete: 10 m (parallel to direction of carriageway).
2)
Minimum width of mass concrete: 2.5 m (minimum 2.375 m unreinforced concrete + minimum
0.125 m bordering kerb width).
3)
Minimum depth of mass concrete: 200 mm.
4)
Where the verge/central reserve length exceeds 20 m, joints in the mass concrete are to be
provided to control cracking.
22

E/B2.2
Additional design guidance - arrangement 1
In addition, the following guidance also applies:
1)
Minimum set back: 1200 mm
2)
Existing bridge parapet to be outside of the working width of the surface mounted safety barrier
3)
Minimum compressive strength of the mass concrete: 30 N/mm2;
4)
Minimum distance from joints or the ends of the mass concrete to the post anchors: 300 mm;
5)
Maximum distance between joints: 6000 mm;
6)
Tensile pull-out testing of individual existing or new anchors is to be carried out in accordance
with CC 400 [Ref 9.N];
7)
The design tensile resistance of the anchor is to be a minimum 65 kN;
8)
The test load to be applied to the anchor is a minimum of 40 kN; and
9)
The rate of testing is to be in accordance with CC 400 [Ref 9.N].

1)
Minimum length of mass concrete: 10 m (parallel to direction of carriageway);
2)
Minimum width of of mass concrete: 1.2 m (minimum 1.075 m unreinforced concrete + minimum
0.125 m bordering kerb width);
3)
Minimum depth of mass concrete: 200 mm;

CD 377 - NINAA Version 2.0.0
Introduction
Introduction
Background
This National Application Annex contains the Department for Infrastructure, Northern Ireland-specific
requirements related to road restraint systems.
This document is an update to CD 377 [Ref 5.N] NINAA and reflects changes to the Overseeing
Organisations' requirements. It also takes account of updated and new EU standards and legislation.
This document gives requirements for road restraint systems and it, together with the associated
RRRAP [Ref 9.N] and RRRAP User Guide [Ref 1.N], assists those involved in determining where road
restraint systems are warranted, and the minimum required parameters.
Assumptions made in the preparation of this document
The assumptions made in GG 101 [Ref 2.N] apply to this document.
This document is written on the basis that road restraint systems are supplied and constructed in
accordance with the Manual of Contract Documents for Highway Works - CC 400 [Ref 4.N], CC 401
[Ref 3.N]and CC 402 [Ref 8.N], and all other works are designed and specified in accordance with the
Design Manual for Roads and Bridges (DMRB).
Mutual recognition
Where there is a requirement in this document for compliance with any part of a British Standard,
technical specification or quality mark, that requirement may be met by compliance with the Mutual
Recognition clause in GG 101 [Ref 2.N].
4
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

CD 377 - NINAA Version 2.0.0
NI/1. Scope (additional to CD 377)
NI/1.
Scope (additional to CD 377)
Implementation and application (CD 377, 1)
NI/1.1
CD 377 [Ref 5.N], clause 1.3 shall not apply.
NI/1.2
This document shall apply to motorways, trunk, and non-trunk roads with permanent speed limits of 50
mph or more and two-way traffic flows of 5,000 annual average daily traffic (AADT) or more:
1)
where the road is a new road;
2)
where the highway cross-section is being altered permanently;
3)
whenever the road restraint system (RRS) is life (serviceable life) expired and needs replacing;
4)
whenever the RRS needs replacing for any other reason;
5)
whenever a hazard is introduced and/or moved, and/or modified, changing the risk in the event of
a collision;
6)
whenever a RRS needs to be dismantled (other than where localised sections need to be
removed to gain access), e.g. during planned maintenance schemes; or
7)
where the Overseeing Organisation is responsible for a structure accommodating vehicles and/or
walking, cycling and horse-riding (WCH) users.
NI/1.3
For the application of clause 1.5 across the NI road network, contact shall be made with the
Overseeing Organisation.
NI/1.4
For trunk, and non-trunk, roads with permanent speed limits of less than 50 mph, or two-way traffic
flows of less than 5,000 annual average daily traffic (AADT), contact shall be made with the Overseeing
Organisation for design standards and guidance on the introduction or replacement of RRS.
5
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

as a design output.

CD 377 - NINAA Version 2.0.0
NI/3. Requirements for permanent safety barriers (a...
NI/3.
Requirements for permanent safety barriers (additional to CD 377)
General requirements for permanent safety barriers (CD 377, 3.1-3.5)
NI/3.1
All new permanent safety barriers shall be maintenance-free for a minimum of 5 years between
scheduled maintenance operations.
Safety barrier provision in central reserves - general (CD 377, 3.79)
NI/3.2
On motorways and all-purpose dual carriageways with a two-way AADT greater or equal to 25,000
vehicles/day where a safety barrier is required in accordance with CD 377 [Ref 5.N] and the distance
Psb to Psb is 10 m or less, the safety barrier shall have a minimum containment level of H1 or H2.
NI/3.3
Safety barriers in the central reserve of motorways and all-purpose dual carriageways with a two-way
AADT greater or equal to 25,000 vehicles/day shall be rigid, have a serviceable life of not less than 50
years and be designed such that after testing in accordance with BS EN 1317-1 [Ref 7.N] and BS EN
1317-2 [Ref 6.N], it does not require realignment, replacement or repair.
NOTE
The installation of a minimum H1 or H2 containment rigid safety barrier is to minimise cross-over
incidents and to reduce the need for safety barriers to be repaired or maintained, and hence minimise
the costs and congestion arising from temporary traffic management and reduce the risk to
maintenance workers.
NI/3.3.1
Where the length of safety barrier to be installed in the central reserve is 500 m or less, an N2
containment level non-rigid safety barrier may be installed.
NI/3.3.2
For upgrades to an existing dual carriageway, a reduction in containment level provision to N2 and/or
the use of a non-rigid safety barrier may be used, following agreement with the Department for
Infrastructure.
7
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

CD 377 - NINAA Version 2.0.0
NI/4. Requirements for vehicle parapets (additional...
NI/4.
Requirements for vehicle parapets (additional to CD 377)
Minimum containment level requirements where the road is carried over or
adjacent to a railway (CD 377, 4.8-4.15)
NI/4.1
Clauses 4.8 to 4.15 inclusive of CD 377 [Ref 5.N] shall not apply.
New and existing bridges, structures and accommodation bridges (CD 377, 4.8-4.15)
NI/4.2
The minimum containment level for a vehicle parapet on a new or existing bridge, structure or
accommodation bridge over a railway shall be determined by a site-specific risk assessment.
NI/4.3
Approval of the risk assessment methodology shall be obtained from the Overseeing Organisation.
NI/4.4
The containment level shall only be provided following consultation with the railway authority and
approval from the Overseeing Organisation.
NI/4.5
Where the need for a normal, high or very high containment level vehicle parapet has been identified,
the nature of the risk, any mitigation measures taken to reduce the risk, and the resulting containment
level required shall be recorded in the Health and Safety file, or similar, for the scheme.
NI/4.6
The minimum vehicle parapet containment level shall be normal containment level (N2).
8

Foreword
Publishing information
This document is published by National Highways on behalf of Transport Scotland.
This document supersedes the previous versions of CD 377 [Ref 6.N] SNAA, which are withdrawn.
Contractual and legal considerations
This document forms part of the works specification. It does not purport to include all the necessary
provisions of a contract. Users are responsible for applying all appropriate documents applicable to
their contract.

CD 377 - SNAA Version 2.1.0
Introduction
Introduction
Background
This National Application Annex contains the Transport Scotland-specific requirements related to road
restraint systems.
This document is an update to previous CD 377 SNAA and reflects changes to the Overseeing
Organisations requirements. It also takes account of updated and new EU standards and legislation.
This document gives requirements for road restraint systems and it, together with the associated
RRRAP [Ref 11.N] and RRRAP User Guide [Ref 1.N], assists those involved in determining where road
restraint systems are warranted, and the minimum required parameters.
Assumptions made in the preparation of this document
The assumptions made in GG 101 [Ref 2.N] apply to this document.
This document is written on the basis that road restraint systems are supplied and constructed in
accordance with the Manual of Contract Documents for Highway Works - CC 400 [Ref 5.N], CC 401
[Ref 4.N]and CC 402 [Ref 10.N], and all other works are designed and specified in accordance with the
Design Manual for Roads and Bridges (DMRB).
Mutual recognition
Where there is a requirement in this document for compliance with any part of a British Standard,
technical specification or quality mark, that requirement may be met by compliance with the Mutual
Recognition clause in GG 101 [Ref 2.N].
4
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

CD 377 - SNAA Version 2.1.0
S/1. Scope (additional to CD 377)
S/1.
Scope (additional to CD 377)
Implementation and application (CD 377, 1.3)
S/1.1
CD 377, clause 1.3 (6) shall not apply.
S/1.1.1
Unless otherwise agreed with the Overseeing Organisation, this document should be applied on the
Overseeing Organisation's motorways and all-purpose trunk roads with a maximum speed limit of 50
mph or more, and two-way traffic flow of 5,000 annual average daily traffic (AADT) or more, and where
a RRS needs to be dismantled on a temporary basis, e.g. during planned maintenance schemes.
S/1.2
This document shall be applied on the Overseeing Organisation's motorways and all-purpose trunk
roads with a maximum speed limit of less than 50 mph, and two-way traffic flow of 5,000 AADT or
more, and where clauses make specific reference to this situation, and:
1)
where the road is a new road;
2)
where the highway cross-section is being altered permanently;
3)
whenever the road restraint system (RRS) is life (serviceable life) expired and needs replacing;
4)
whenever the RRS needs replacing for any other reason;
5)
whenever a hazard is introduced and/or moved, and/or modified, changing the risk in the event of
a collision; or
6)
where the Overseeing Organisation is responsible for a structure accommodating vehicles and/or
walking, cycling and horse-riding (WCH) users.
S/1.2.1
On the Overseeing Organisation's motorways and all-purpose trunk roads with a maximum speed limit
of 50 mph or more, and two-way traffic flow of less than 5,000 AADT, all requirements and
recommendations in CD 377 should be applied as recommendations, with the principles of SFAIRP.
6
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

PAGE 173 of 199

CD 377 - SNAA Version 2.1.0
S/2. General requirements for road restraint syste...
S/2.
General requirements for road restraint systems (additional to CD
377)
Hazard identification and risk mitigation for road restraint systems (CD 377, 2.2)
S/2.1
CD 377, clause 2.2 shall not apply.
S/2.2
On the all-purpose trunk road network where the speed limit is less than 50 mph and/or the two-way
traffic flow is less than 5,000 AADT, a risk assessment which is acceptable to the Overseeing
Organisation, shall be undertaken to determine whether RRS is necessary and the minimum
containment and performance levels for the RRS.
NOTE 1
Local authority guidance such as the DfT UKRLG 'Design & Maintenance Guidance for Local Authority
Roads: Provision of Road Restraint Systems on Local Authority Roads' D&MG LHA [Ref 1.I] provides
advice and alternatives to the RRRAP to road authorities and their designers when considering the
introduction or replacement of RRSs on roads with low traffic flows and/or low traffic speeds.
NOTE 2
Guidance on the specification of vehicle restraint systems on the approach to and across structures on
low speed and/or low flow roads can be found in Appendix B of CD 377.
Environmental requirements (CD 377, 2.56)
S/2.3
In accordance with CD 377 [Ref 6.N], in areas where environmental conditions that will affect the
choice and positioning of the safety barrier, any restrictions on the type or material for the barrier shall
be included as a design output.
NOTE
Environmental considerations can also include a local prevalence of wildlife, so a suitable choice of
barrier can ensure that animals are able to leave the carriageway and are not trapped by an
inappropriate system.
7
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

CD 377 - SNAA Version 2.1.0
S/3. Requirements for permanent safety barriers (a...
S/3.
Requirements for permanent safety barriers (additional to CD 377)
Minimum containment levels (CD 377, 3.6-3.7, 3.47-3.48 and 3.64)
S/3.1
In accordance with CD 377 [Ref 6.N], minimum containment levels for permanent safety barriers shall
be as defined in clauses 3.6, 3.7, 3.47, 3.48 and 3.64.
S/3.1.1
Where higher or very high containment level systems are required, an 'L' level containment system
compliant with BS EN 1317-2 [Ref 8.N] may be used in place of an 'H' level system.
NOTE
Products with an 'L' level are preferred where these are available and meet the contract performance
requirements.
Safety barrier provision in central reserves - general (CD 377, 3.78)
S/3.2
On motorways and all-purpose dual carriageways with a two-way AADT greater or equal to 25,000
vehicles/day, where a VRS is required on the central reserve under the other criteria set out in CD 377
[Ref 6.N], and the distance Psb to Psb is 10 metres or less, a barrier of higher or very high containment
level shall be provided.
8
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

CD 377 - SNAA Version 2.1.0
S/4. Requirements for vehicle parapets (additional...
S/4.
Requirements for vehicle parapets (additional to CD 377)
Minimum containment levels where the road is not carried over or adjacent to a
railway (CD 377, 4.2 and 4.3)
S/4.1
In accordance with CD 377 [Ref 6.N], minimum containment levels for vehicle parapets where the road
is not carried over or adjacent to a railway shall be as defined in clauses 4.2 and 4.3.
S/4.1.1
Where higher or very high containment level systems are required, an 'L' level containment system
compliant with BS EN 1317-2 [Ref 8.N] may be used in place of an 'H' level system.
NOTE
Products with an 'L' level are preferred where these are available and meet the contract performance
requirements.
Minimum containment level requirements where the road is carried over or
adjacent to a railway (CD 377, 4.8 and 4.9)
S/4.2
In accordance with CD 377 [Ref 6.N], minimum containment levels for vehicle parapets where the road
is carried over or adjacent to a railway (except on accommodation bridges) shall be as defined in
clauses 4.8 and 4.9.
S/4.2.1
Wherever reference is made in clauses 4.8 and 4.9 to 'H4a' containment, this may be extended to
include 'H4a or L4a' containment.
NOTE
Products with an 'L' level are preferred where these are available and meet the contract performance
requirements.
9
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

S/5. Requirements for transitions
S/5.
Requirements for transitions
Minimum containment levels (additional to CD 377, Clause 7.10)
S/5.1
In accordance with CD 377 [Ref 6.N], minimum containment levels for transitions shall be as defined in
7.10.
S/5.1.1
Where higher or very high containment level systems are required, an 'L' level containment system
compliant with DD ENV 1317-4 2002 [Ref 3.N] or PD CEN/TR 1317-10 [Ref 7.N] may be used in place
of an 'H' level system.
NOTE
Products with an 'L' level are preferred where these are available and meet the contract performance
requirements.
10

S/6. Requirements for temporary vehicle restraint ...
S/6.
Requirements for temporary vehicle restraint systems (additional
to CD 377)
Minimum containment levels for temporary safety barriers (CD 377, 11.26-11.27,
and 11.33-11.34)
S/6.1
In accordance with CD 377 [Ref 6.N], minimum containment levels for temporary safety barriers shall
be as defined in clauses 11.26, 11.27, 11.33 and 11.34.
S/6.1.1
Where higher or very high containment level systems are required, an 'L' level containment system
compliant with BS EN 1317-2 [Ref 8.N] may be used in place of an 'H' level system.
NOTE
Products with an 'L' level are preferred where these are available and meet the contract performance
requirements.
Minimum containment levels for temporary transitions (CD 377, 11.75)
S/6.2
In accordance with CD 377 [Ref 6.N], minimum containment levels for temporary safety barriers shall
be as defined in Clause 11.75.
S/6.2.1
Where higher or very high containment level systems are required, an 'L' level containment system
compliant with DD ENV 1317-4 2002 [Ref 3.N]or PD CEN/TR 1317-10 [Ref 7.N] may be used in place
of an 'H' level system.
NOTE
Products with an 'L' level are preferred where these are available and meet the contract performance
requirements.

CD 377 - SNAA Version 2.1.0
S/7. Cattle grids (additional to CD 377)
S/7.
Cattle grids (additional to CD 377)
Siting of cattle grids (CD 377, 15.3)
S/7.1
In accordance with CD 377 [Ref 6.N], cattle grids and any associated by-pass shall be located within
highway land unless a legal agreement with the relevant land owner has been entered into.
NOTE
For cattle grids to be located outside of the public road boundary, a legal agreement is entered into
under Section 46 of The Roads (Scotland) Act ( UKPGA 1984/54 [Ref 9.N]).
12
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

CD 377 - WNAA Version 2.0.0
Introduction
Introduction
Background
This National Application Annex contains the Welsh Government-specific requirements related to road
restraint systems.
This document is an update to CD 377 [Ref 8.N] WNAA and reflects changes to the Welsh
Government's requirements. It also takes account of updated and new EU standards.
This document gives requirements for road restraint systems and it, together with the associated
RRRAPfW [Ref 11.N]and RRRAP User Guide [Ref 2.N], assists those involved in determining where
road restraint systems are warranted, and the minimum required parameters.
Assumptions made in the preparation of this document
The assumptions made in GG 101 [Ref 3.N] apply to this document.
This document is written on the basis that road restraint systems are supplied and constructed in
accordance with the Manual of Contract Documents for Highway Works - CC 400 [Ref 7.N], CC 401
[Ref 6.N]and CC 402 [Ref 10.N], and all other works are designed and specified in accordance with the
Design Manual for Roads and Bridges (DMRB).
Mutual recognition
Where there is a requirement in this document for compliance with any part of a British Standard,
technical specification or quality mark, that requirement may be met by compliance with the Mutual
Recognition clause in GG 101 [Ref 3.N].
4

CD 377 - WNAA Version 2.0.0
Terms and definitions
Terms and definitions
Term
Definition
Routine
1. For maintenance: limited to cyclic maintenance
work activity as detailed within the Wales Trunk
Road Maintenance Manual PAG 119/23 [Ref 2.I];
2. Safety critical: Category 1 defect reinstatement
as described in the Wales Trunk Road Maintenance
Manual PAG 119/23 [Ref 2.I].
Walking, cycling and horse-riding and
wheeling (WCH) routes
All routes within the scope of CD 143 [Ref 1.N]
which are used by walkers, cyclists, horse riders
and wheelers.
Wheeling
The use of wheelchairs, pushchairs, prams, etc.

PAGE 189 of 199
======================================================================
CD 377 - WNAA Version 2.0.0
W/1. Scope (additional to CD 377)
W/1.
Scope (additional to CD 377)
Implementation and application (CD 377, 1)
W/1.1
CD 377 [Ref 8.N], clauses 1.3 and 1.4 shall not apply.
W/1.2
This document shall apply to all motorways and trunk roads across the Wales road network.
NOTE
Guidance on the implementation of CD 377 [Ref 8.N] and this document can be found in PAG 119/23
[Ref 2.I].
W/1.3
This document shall be applied:
1)
where the road is a new road;
2)
where the highway cross-section is being altered permanently;
3)
whenever the road restraint system (RRS) is life (serviceable life) expired and needs replacing;
4)
whenever the RRS needs replacing for any other reason;
5)
whenever a hazard is introduced and/or moved, and/or modified, changing the risk in the event of
a collision;
6)
whenever a RRS needs to be dismantled (other than where localised sections need to be
removed to gain access), e.g. during planned maintenance schemes; or
7)
where the Welsh Government is responsible for a structure accommodating vehicles and/or
walking, cycling and horse-riding (WCH) users.
W/1.3.1
Unless otherwise agreed with the Welsh Government, this document should also be applied:
1)
when other works (excluding routine maintenance and safety critical interventions) are being
carried out near a hazard that is currently without provision, or near an existing RRS that does not
meet the requirements of this document (for example, with regard to its containment level,
normalised working width class, normalised vehicle intrusion class);
2)
when other works (excluding routine maintenance and safety critical interventions) are being
carried out near an existing vehicle restraint system (VRS) which is life (service life) expired;
3)
when other works (excluding routine maintenance and safety critical interventions) are being
carried out near an existing RRS that has less than 5 years serviceable life remaining and no
other major maintenance works are planned during the remaining life of the existing RRS.
W/1.3.2
Like-for-like renewal may be used where:
1)
localised sections need to be temporarily removed to gain access;
2)
repair work is required; or
3)
the RRS is required to be replaced due to incident damage.
NOTE
More details on localised sections which need to be temporarily removed to gain access can be found
in Section 10.
Replacement of welded angle beams (CD 377, 1.6)
W/1.4
CD 377 [Ref 8.N], clause 1.6 shall not apply.
W/1.5
Where terminals which incorporate welded angle beams are being removed and/or replaced, the
welded angle beams shall be replaced with a terminal in accordance with Section 6, or a terminal in
accordance with the NPSBS v1 2005 [Ref 4.N] drawings, and not on a like-for-like basis, unless agreed
by the Welsh Government.
NOTE
In some cases, terminals might not be replaced at all if, for example, a gap is to be closed due to the
presence of unprotected hazards in advance of, or following, the terminal which is to be removed.
7
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

CD 377 - WNAA Version 2.0.0
W/3. Requirements for permanent safety barriers (a...
W/3.
Requirements for permanent safety barriers (additional to CD 377)
Normalised working width classes and normalised vehicle intrusion classes for
permanent safety barriers (CD 377, 3.13)
W/3.1
The NOTE to clause 3.13 of CD 377 [Ref 8.N] shall not apply.
Motorcyclist protection devices (CD 377, 3.42)
W/3.2
Clause 3.42 of CD 377 [Ref 8.N] shall not apply.
Safety barrier provision in central reserves - general (CD 377, 3.79)
Safety barrier provision in central reserves of new roads
W/3.3
On new motorways and dual carriageways with a predicted two-way annual average daily traffic
(AADT) greater than or equal to 25,000 vehicles/day, where a safety barrier is required in accordance
with CD 377 [Ref 8.N], and the distance Psb to Psb is 10 metres or less, and the length of safety barrier
to be installed is greater than 500 m, a rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50
years and a minimum containment level of H1 shall be installed in the central reserve.
NOTE
The installation of a safety barrier with a minimum containment level of H1 is to reduce the risk of
cross-over incidents.
W/3.4
For all other new roads, a safety barrier with a minimum containment level of N2 shall be installed in the
central reserve.
Safety barrier provision in central reserves of existing roads
W/3.5
On existing motorways and dual carriageways with a two-way annual average daily traffic (AADT)
greater than or equal to 25,000 vehicles/day, where a safety barrier is required in accordance with CD
377 [Ref 8.N], the distance Psb to Psb is 10 metres or less, and the length of safety barrier to be
installed is greater than 500 m, the safety barrier in the central reserve shall have a minimum
containment level of H1.
NOTE
The installation of a safety barrier with a minimum containment level of H1 is to reduce the risk of
cross-over incidents.
W/3.6
On existing motorways and dual carriageways where the length of safety barrier to be installed in the
central reserve is 500 m or less, a safety barrier with a minimum containment level of N2 shall be
installed.
W/3.6.1
The inclusion of a 'rigid' or a 'non rigid' safety barrier in the central reserve, should be supported by an
evidence-based business case, comparing options.
W/3.6.2
The serviceable life of the safety barrier which is to be installed in the central reserve, should be
supported by an evidence-based business case, comparing options.
W/3.7
Any evidence-based business case shall be recorded and agreed with the Welsh Government.
NOTE
The installation of a rigid safety barrier with a serviceable life of not less than 50 years is to reduce the
need for safety barriers to be repaired following an impact by an errant vehicle and hence, minimise the
congestion arising from temporary traffic management and reduce the risk to maintenance workers.
W/3.8
Factors to include in an evidence-based business case shall include:
1)
the AADT of the road;
2)
the number of HGVs using the road;
3)
the number of cross-over incidents;
4)
the number of repairs to the central reserve safety barrier;
5)
environmental impacts  habitat segregation, carbon cost etc; and
9
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

6)
any other factors increasing the risk of an impact with the safety barrier in the central reserve.

CD 377 - WNAA Version 2.0.0
W/5. Requirements for permanent terminals (additio...
W/5.
Requirements for permanent terminals (additional to CD 377)
Performance class for terminals (CD 377, 6.3-6.6)
W/5.1
Where it is necessary to replace or renew an existing P1 terminal which faces oncoming traffic on a
road with a speed limit of 50 mph or more, and two-way traffic flow of 5,000 annual average daily traffic
(AADT) or more, the terminal shall be replaced with with a terminal with a performance class of T110 or
T110/1 as defined by PD CEN/TS 1317-7 [Ref 9.N], or P4 as defined by DD ENV 1317-4 2002 [Ref
5.N] provided that:
1)
the existing safety barrier to which the terminal will be connected has at least 5 years of
serviceable life remaining;
2)
the replacement terminal is capable of providing any anchorage which is required by the safety
barrier; and
3)
the Welsh Government has received and approved a case for change technical note which has
identified all of the non compliance aspects of the current safety barrier.
12
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 377 Version 5.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

CD 377 - WNAA Version 2.0.0
W/6. Requirements for pedestrian restraint systems...
W/6.
Requirements for pedestrian restraint systems (additional to CD
377)
General requirements for pedestrian restraint systems (CD 377, 9.21)
General requirements for all pedestrian guardrails
W/6.1
Clause 9.21 of CD 377 [Ref 8.N] shall not apply.
General requirements for pedestrian restraint systems not located adjacent to
WCH routes (CD 377, 9.67)
Pedestrian restraint systems located adjacent to maintenance footpaths
W/6.2
Pedestrian restraint systems shall be provided adjacent to maintenance footpaths at the top of
embankments with
1)
a height of 0.5m or greater; and
2)
a gradient steeper than 1 in 2.
W/6.2.1
The requirements for pedestrian restraint systems provided adjacent to maintenance footpaths at the
top of embankments may be relaxed subject to risk assessment in accordance with Welsh Government
Risk Assessment process.
NOTE
The Welsh Government Risk Assessment process is available on request from Welsh Government.

W/7. Requirements for cattle grids (additional to ...
W/7.
Requirements for cattle grids (additional to CD 377)
Siting of cattle grids (CD 377, 15.3)
W/7.1
A check shall be made that cattle grids and any associated by-pass are to be located within highway
land, unless a legal agreement with the relevant land owner has been entered in to.
W/7.1.1
New cattle grids should be located within the highway boundary.
NOTE
For cattle grids to be located on non-highway land, a legal agreement is entered into under Section 87
of the UKPGA 1980/66 [Ref 1.I].
